William M. Klein wrote:
> For those (if any) who care, the latest (August 2009) draft of the ongoing 
> revision of the ISO COBOL Standard can be found from the PL22.4 home page at:
…[3 more quoted lines elided]…
>   http://www.cobolstandard.info/j4/files/std.zip

Thanks, Bill. There is much skepticism here about the new standard,
and about COBOL standards in general, and I understand why; and
perhaps we'll never see a fully-compliant implementation of the new
standard. (I'm not even sure if our COBOL is fully compliant with
2002, when building with the various 2002 directives.) But I for one
like to see what the committee is thinking about, and how they'd like
to see the language evolve.
```

##### ↳ ↳ Re: DRAFT COBOL revision

- **From:** Emerson <emersonlopes@gmail.com>
- **Date:** 2009-09-22T07:42:53-07:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<83d15920-1599-4bda-8992-1167f12fb904@h30g2000vbr.googlegroups.com>`
- **References:** `<obZrm.19835$Xg3.19307@en-nntp-04.dc1.easynews.com> <h8r72l41d46@news2.newsguy.com>`

```
Hi,

There has been more activity in the committe in the last 5 years than
in the 15 year before it, nonethless many things that could led Cobol
into a new reality has been disregarded over the years (scoped
variables, var length strings, removal of number levels for object
references, user defined functions, web forms support, etc)

Some things were implemented here and there by this or that cobol
vendor, but the lack of a unified approach is really killing the
language. Why the committe cannot boldy go where no committe has gone
before? to keep things as they are? That's silly...every day I hear
that this or that company is shutting down their mainframes and moving
their Cobol into Windows/Linux in order to more easily kill it. A
couple weeks ago I was told that a class entity in Rio de Janeiro is
spending several million dollars to get rid of their cobol systems
(rewriting them in Java). When they were told that there were many
available cobol compilers capable to create web aware applications
their reaction was disbelief saying "there is no cobol standard for
the web"...and they are right...

Many people out there says that the main reason why Cobol has been
created was never achived "to be ease to understand and maintain".
That's silly too. HTML is not ease to read or maintain, but is widely
used by everyone. So, if we have to sacrifice some clarity in order to
short the number of lines that we write, WHY NOT?

Consider the following code:

CLASS-ID. TwitterPost AS "CoolThings.TwitterPost".

   environment division.
       configuration section.
           repository.
               class     SystemWebHttpUtility      as
"System.Web.HttpUtility"
                class     SystemString              as "System.String"
                class     SystemInteger             as "System.Int32"
                class     NetworkCredential         as
"System.Net.NetworkCredential"
                class     NetWebRequest             as
"System.Net.WebRequest"
                class     NetWebResponse            as
"System.Net.WebResponse"
                class     WebHeaderCollection       as
"System.Net.WebHeaderCollection"
                class     ClassByteArray            as "System.Byte[]"
                class     SystemTextEncoding        as
"System.Text.Encoding"
                class     SystemIOStream            as
"System.IO.Stream"
                class     SystemIOStreamReader      as
"System.IO.StreamReader"
                class     ClassServicePointManager  as
"System.Net.ServicePointManager"

                class     ClassWebException         as
"System.Net.WebException"

                property  Credentials               as "Credentials"
                property  ContentType               as "ContentType"
                property  ContentLenght             as "ContentLength"
                property  ArrayLength               as "Length"
                property  RequestMethod             as "Method"
                property  Headers                   as "Headers"
                property  Expect100Continue         as
"Expect100Continue".

*> Instance's data and methods
   object.
      data division.
           working-storage section.

      procedure division.

            method-id. PostRequest as "PostRequest".

                data division.

                    working-storage section.

                    01 WebHttpUtility        usage object reference
SystemWebHttpUtility.
                    01 servicePointManager   usage object reference
ClassServicePointManager.
                    01 request               usage object reference
NetWebRequest.
                    01 response              usage object reference
NetWebResponse.
                    01 requestCredential     usage object reference
NetworkCredential.
                    01 requestHeaders        usage object reference
WebHeaderCollection.
                    01 byteArray             usage object reference
ClassByteArray.
                    01 utf8Encoding          usage object reference
SystemTextEncoding.
                    01 requestStream         usage object reference
SystemIOStream.
                    01 responseStream        usage object reference
SystemIOStream.
                    01 reader                usage object reference
SystemIOStreamReader.
                    01 bytesLength           usage object reference
SystemInteger.

                    01 webException          usage object reference
ClassWebException.

                    01 twitterSTatus         usage object reference
SystemString.

                     linkage section.
                     01 url                usage object reference
SystemString.
                     01 userName           usage object reference
SystemString.
                     01 userPassword       usage object reference
SystemString.
                     01 userText           usage object reference
SystemString.
                     01 result             usage object reference
SystemString.

                 procedure division using url, userName, UserPassword,
userText returning result.

                     *> http://blogs.msdn.com/shitals/archive/2008/12/27/9254245.aspx

                     set Expect100Continue of
ClassServicePointManager   to   b"0"

                     invoke NetWebRequest "Create" using url returning
request

                     invoke NetworkCredential "NEW" using userName,
userPassword returning requestCredential

                     set    Credentials   of request   to
requestCredential
                     set    ContentType   of request   to
"application/x-www-form-urlencoded"
                     set    RequestMethod of request   to  "POST"

                     set    requestHeaders             to  Headers of
request

                     invoke requestHeaders "Add" using "X-Twitter-
Client",  "OO Cobol"
                     invoke requestHeaders "Add" using "X-Twitter-
Version", "1.0"
                     invoke requestHeaders "Add" using "X-Twitter-
URL",     "http://www.100coolthings.net"

                     invoke SystemTextEncoding "GetEncoding" using
n"UTF-8" returning utf8Encoding

                     invoke SystemWebHttpUtility "UrlEncode" using
userText returning userText

                     set    twitterStatus  to
SystemString::"Concat"("status=", userText)

                     invoke utf8Encoding "GetBytes" using
twitterStatus returning byteArray

                     set    ContentLenght of request   to  ArrayLength
of byteArray

                    invoke request "GetRequestStream" returning
requestStream

                    set    bytesLength                to  ArrayLength
of byteArray

                    invoke requestStream "Write" using byteArray, 0,
bytesLength

                    try
                        invoke request "GetResponse" returning
response

                    catch webException
                          continue
                    end-try

                    invoke response "GetResponseStream" returning
responseStream

                    invoke SystemIOStreamReader "NEW" using
responseStream returning reader

                    invoke reader "ReadToEnd" returning result.

           end method PostRequest.
   end object.
END CLASS TwitterPost.

About 50% of the code(!) is dedicated to declare classes and types...

Why can't we do something like:

CLASS-ID. TwitterPost AS "CoolThings.TwitterPost".

    repository.
          IMPORT "System.*".

*> Instance's data and methods
   object.
            method-id. PostRequest as "PostRequest".

               working-storage section.

                    webHttpUtility        AS "Web.HttpUtility".
                    servicePointManager   AS
"Net.ServicePointManager".
                    request               AS "Net.WebRequest".
                    requestCredential     AS "Network.Credential".
                    requestHeaders        AS "WebHeader.Collection".
                    byteArray             AS ARRAY OF "Byte".
                    utf8Encoding          AS "Text.Encoding".
                    requestStream         AS "IO.Stream".
                    responseStream        AS "IO.Stream".
                    reader                AS "IO.StreamReader".
                    bytesLength           AS "Integer".
                    webException          AS "Net.WebException".
                    twitterSTatus         AS "String".

                 procedure division using url               AS
"String",
                                          userName          AS
"String",
                                          userPassword      AS
"String",
                                          userText          AS
"String",
                                          returning result  AS
"String".

                     set "Expect100Continue" of
ClassServicePointManager   to   FALSE

                     set  request                      to
NetWebRequest::Create(url)

                     set    "Credentials"   of request   to
NetworkCredential::NEW(userName, userPassword)
                     set    "ContentType"   of request   to
"application/x-www-form-urlencoded"
                     set    "RequestMethod" of request   to  "POST"

                     request::Headers::Add("X-Twitter-Client",  "OO
Cobol")
                     request::Headers::Add("X-Twitter-Version",
"1.0")
                     request::Headers::Add("X-Twitter-URL", "http://
www.100coolthings.net")

                     set utf8Encoding     to  TextEncoding::GetEncoding
(n"UTF-8")

                     set userText         to  WebHttpUtility::UrlEncode
(userText)

                     set twitterStatus    to
String::"Concat"("status=", userText)

                     set byteArray        to  utf8Encoding::GetBytes
(twitterStatus)

                     set "ContentLenght" of request   to  "Length" of
byteArray

                     set  requestStream   to  request::GetRequestStream
()

                     requestStream::Write(byteArray, 0, "Length" of
byteArray)

                     set reader to IOStreamReader::NEW
(request::GetResponse()::GetResponseStream())

                     invoke reader "ReadToEnd" returning result.

           end method PostRequest.
   end object.
END CLASS TwitterPost.

Syntax is greatly simplified, specially the repository x working-
storage relationship. Nonetheless, it still feels like Cobol, it still
does the job, but it requires over 40% less coding, and I pretty sure
that we could improve it a lot.

Some stuff above is implemented by Micro Focus, but Fujitsu does not
(nor other Cobol vendors) because there is no real standard in this
very moment.

I hope the next movement of the committe (that includes java/.Net/etc
frameworks support) aims less coding...

Regards, Emerson

```
"The committee" (actually the full ANSI and ISO system) have already done some 
of the things you are asking about.

User defined functions have been in the approved Standard since 2002. "Scoped 
variables" have been available sine the '85 Standard introduced nested programs.

There is a WORLD of difference between what is in the Standard (especially the 
'02 Standard) and what any compiler vendor feels is "worth implementing".

As long as standardization needs to follow the rules of ISO (or ANSI), there is 
simply NO WAY  that any feature can be made "official" in less than five years 
after the date when works begins on it.  If you look at the XML TR (for example) 
it was sufficiently "late" in being approved that the "need" for it had already 
passed.
```

Hi,

I made a lengthy post here that never appeared. Maybe it was better
this way, saving you to read my confuse explanation. :)

Anyways, The only part that was worth to mention is scoped variable.
85 scoped variable is a very disappointing definition of it, besides
in OO realm external and/or global has no meaning...

This is what I was talking about:

perform until false
        invoke Order "NEW" returning myOrder as ClientOrder

        myOrder::"Total" > 0 ? continue : exit perform

end-perform

No working-storage section for myOrder and no myOrder exists outside
of perform scope

Another example

if (order::"Date" < currentDate) then
    set myClient as <Client>     to  order::"client"
    display client::"name"
end-if

no "myClient" exists outside of "if" scope.

Could it be done for cobol types? Maybe:

if (order::"total" < currentDate) then
   set  counter as <pic 9(10)>   to  zeros
   perform until counter > 1000
           add 1  to  counter
   end-perform
end-if

Could it be done? Course! make sense? I believe so! Besides, it could
be also used to implement Generics very easily...think about it :)

Regards, Emerson

```
That is certainly interesting.  What you are looking for is local variables
that are local not only to a "program" (or a method), but are actually local
to a block.  I guess we could call them "block local variables"!  :-)

Are they available in any existing Cobol compiler, or is this just syntax
you came up with?

Are you also wanting the C-like "ternary" operator, where:

myOrder::"Total" > 0 ? continue : exit perform

Is the same as this?

if myOrder::"Total" > 0
    continue
else
    exit program
end-if

Not sure I'd go that far, but...
Anyway, I'm not sure you've used it correctly.  Even in C isn't it a
requirement that the values after the question mark, separated by the colon,
are expressions and not statements?  For example, I don't think the
following C (well, C# I guess) is valid:

myOrder.Total() > 0 ? break : return;

...because break and return are statements, not expressions.

I'm only guessing.  I don't have a C# compiler here to test it.

Frank
```

###### ↳ ↳ ↳ Re: DRAFT COBOL revision

_(thread depth: 7)_

- **From:** Emerson <emersonlopes@gmail.com>
- **Date:** 2009-09-30T09:46:01-07:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<30b5dadb-61fa-4ab5-994f-3c70cf5bbc82@c28g2000yqd.googlegroups.com>`
- **References:** `<obZrm.19835$Xg3.19307@en-nntp-04.dc1.easynews.com> <h8r72l41d46@news2.newsguy.com> <83d15920-1599-4bda-8992-1167f12fb904@h30g2000vbr.googlegroups.com> <_z9um.40309$Hw.10121@en-nntp-08.dc1.easynews.com> <psbib55bn48gfkvmkl3qte4t3sgloqv537@4ax.com> <407560d7-1998-44ae-9a5f-eb810cdd483c@w36g2000yqm.googlegroups.com> <a059aba9-692e-44eb-a66e-162bf8c1a48e@g22g2000prf.googlegroups.com>`

```
To code Cobol in Perl-style is almost a criminal offense :) I just
want to create smaller applications in Cobol, that´s all.

Regarding local variables, I'm sorry, I cannot see why do I need to
predefine everything. This make no sense, specially when it comes to
external types (.Net/Java). The code size is almost multiplied by 2 in
such cases (2x ugh) (repository + working-storage).

Regarding my ternary example, Frank is right regarding rhe very
definition of a ternary , only expressions are supported.

Regarding the syntax to create local variables it was something that
occured me after spend a lot of time dealing with Cobol verbosity. For
instance, the following example serializes an OO Cobol class in XML
format. Notice that over 50% is dedicated to predefine items...that's
too much and add too little value:

       IDENTIFICATION DIVISION.
       PROGRAM-ID. MAIN AS "ConsoleApplication8.Main".
       ENVIRONMENT DIVISION.
       CONFIGURATION SECTION.
       SPECIAL-NAMES.
       REPOSITORY.
       class  SystemXmlSerializer as
"System.Xml.Serialization.XmlSerializer"
       class  SystemConsole       as "System.Console"
       class  SystemTextWriter    as "System.IO.TextWriter"
       class  SystemStringWriter  as "System.IO.StringWriter"
       class  SystemType          as "System.Type"
       class  ClassContratado     as
"CoolThings.OOCobolAndFlex.SD02M1P"
           PROPERTY PROP-OUT AS "Out"
           PROPERTY PROP-NOME AS "nome"
           PROPERTY PROP-ENDERECO AS "endereco"
           PROPERTY PROP-BAIRRO AS "bairro"
           PROPERTY PROP-CEP AS "cep"
           PROPERTY PROP-CGC AS "cgc"
           PROPERTY PROP-CODIGO AS "codigo"
           PROPERTY PROP-EMIT AS "emit"
           PROPERTY PROP-ESTADO AS "estado"
           PROPERTY PROP-IDENT AS "ident"
           PROPERTY PROP-MUNICIPIO AS "municipio"
           PROPERTY PROP-TELEFONES AS "telefones".

       DATA DIVISION.
       WORKING-STORAGE SECTION.
           01 console usage object reference SystemConsole.
           01 textWriter usage object reference SystemTextWriter.
           01 stringWriter usage object reference SystemStringWriter.
           01 xmlSerializer usage object reference
SystemXmlSerializer.
           01 contratado usage object reference ClassContratado.
           01 contratadoType usage object reference SystemType.
           01 xml pic n(1024).
       PROCEDURE DIVISION.

        invoke ClassContratado "NEW" returning contratado

        set  PROP-NOME OF contratado to  "John Doe"
        set  PROP-ENDERECO OF contratado to "Neverland"
        set  PROP-BAIRRO OF contratado to "My neighborhood"
        set  PROP-CEP OF contratado    to 20000
        move zeros                    to PROP-CGC OF contratado
        set  PROP-CODIGO OF contratado to 1
        set  PROP-EMIT OF contratado   to "Secretaria de segurança"
        set  PROP-ESTADO OF contratado to "RJ"
        set  PROP-IDENT OF contratado  to "101010101"
        set  PROP-MUNICIPIO OF contratado to "Rio de Janeiro"
        set  PROP-TELEFONES OF contratado to "(21)2121-2121"

        invoke contratado "GetType" returning contratadoType

        invoke SystemStringWriter "NEW"  returning textWriter

        set    textWriter  to  PROP-OUT OF SystemConsole

        invoke SystemXmlSerializer "NEW" using contratadoType
returning xmlSerializer

        invoke xmlSerializer "Serialize" using  textWriter,
contratado.

        invoke textWriter "Flush"

       END PROGRAM MAIN.


Notice that throught the logic some items are used only a couple of
times. It could be rewrite as:


       IDENTIFICATION DIVISION.
       PROGRAM-ID. MAIN AS "ConsoleApplication8.Main".
       ENVIRONMENT DIVISION.
       CONFIGURATION SECTION.
       SPECIAL-NAMES.
       REPOSITORY.
           ClassContratado     as "CoolThings.OOCobolAndFlex.SD02M1P".

       DATA DIVISION.
       WORKING-STORAGE SECTION.
           01 contratado usage object reference ClassContratado.
           01 xml pic n(1024).

       PROCEDURE DIVISION.

        set  "nome" OF contratado      to  "John Doe"
        set  "endereco" OF contratado  to "Neverland"
        set  "bairro" OF contratado    to "My neighborhood"
        set  "cep" OF contratado       to 20000
        move zeros                     to PROP-CGC OF contratado
        set  "codigo" OF contratado    to 1
        set  "emit" OF contratado      to "Secretaria de segurança"
        set  "estado" OF contratado    to "RJ"
        set  "ident" OF contratado     to "101010101"
        set  "municipio" OF contratado to "Rio de Janeiro"
        set  "telefones" OF contratado to "(21)2121-2121"

        invoke contratado "GetType" returning contratadoType as
<System.Type>

        invoke <System.IO.StringWriter> "NEW"  returning textWriter as
<System.IO.TextWriter>

        set    stringWriter  to  "Out" of <System.Console>

        invoke SystemXmlSerializer "NEW" using contratadoType
returning xmlSerializer as <System.XML.XmlSerializer>

        invoke xmlSerializer "Serialize" using  textWriter,
contratado.
        invoke textWriter "Flush"

       END PROGRAM MAIN.

40% less code and still feels as Cobol...now you don't need to go back
to both working-storage and repository the object reference of a type.
You gain productivity! Is this so wrong?


Regards, Emerson

On Oct 1, 5:46 am, Emerson <emersonlo...@gmail.com> wrote:
> To code Cobol in Perl-style is almost a criminal offense :) I just
> want to create smaller applications in Cobol, that´s all.

Perl can be written several completely different ways. You want to add
another different way to Cobol.


> Regarding local variables, I'm sorry, I cannot see why do I need to
> predefine everything. This make no sense,

By predefining everything you are giving information to the compiler
about what is allowed in the code. If you can just use a name without
predefining it then how can the compiler know whether that was not
just a typing error.

> specially when it comes to
> external types (.Net/Java). The code size is almost multiplied by 2 in
> such cases (2x ugh) (repository + working-storage).

If it is an external type then introspection (in some other language)
should allow you to know what is there. It should be a simple matter
to generate the definitions and then COPY them as required. This is
what is (or should be) done with FDs and SQL.

> Regarding my ternary example, Frank is right regarding rhe very
> definition of a ternary , only expressions are supported.
…[5 more quoted lines elided]…
> too much and add too little value:


So don't use Cobol. There is no point in using Cobol - the COMMON ...
- when you then make it uncommon by restricting it to Windows.NET
only. You may as well do it in C# and be done with it.

Personally I write XML using templating. Actually the programs neither
know nor care that it is XML, it may be HTML, or CSV, or text or
EDIFACT (and often is determined by the user).

Be that as it may, it should be easy to generate the required COPY
books in such a way that the next program can also use them.


>        IDENTIFICATION DIVISION.
>        PROGRAM-ID. MAIN AS "ConsoleApplication8.Main".
…[178 more quoted lines elided]…
>
```

###### ↳ ↳ ↳ Re: DRAFT COBOL revision

- **From:** Paul <paul-nospamatall.raulerson@mac.com>

Gads - all this seems to be an incredibly complex way to do a simple thing.
How for instance would you just write a hello world web page out from a
simple CGI program?

Today, with some compilers, it is as simple as:

 Identification Division.
 Program-ID. Hello.
 Procedure Division.
     Display 'Content-type: text/html'
     Display ''
     Display 'Hello World'
      goback.

How complex do you propose to make it?

How can you make COBOL simple to use for Web2 applications?
About the best way I have seen to do this is what COBOLSCRIPT
did. Simple, fast, and pretty effective.

If you want object orientation, keep it simple!

    Move MY-NAME to textbox.MyName.Text

Or something like that.

```
Wow, so many twisted mouths and no love at all.

Pete/Riplin

There will be no "Cobol community" as you know in ten years from now.
A new generation, whether you like it or not will take the helm and
keep current Cobol applications running because THERE IS NO MONEY to
convert legacy code into C#, Java or anything else. A good amount of
investment will flow into rehosting projects (Mainframe->whatever,
Unix->Windows, Windows->Linux) in order to reduce costs and also into
projects to add modern business needs into existing applications(such
as SOA/messaging/workflow etc). My point is that a lot of those
features requires more code than the necessary, like this web service
below (notice that over 60% of the code is dedicated to predefine
stuff):

class-id. OOCobol as "OOCobol"  inherits         ClassWebService
                                custom-attribute WebService,
                                                 WSBinding.
 environment division.
     configuration section.
         special-names.
             custom-attribute            WebService
             class                       ClassWebServiceAttribute
             property propNamespace  is  N"http://www.redrails.net/"

             custom-attribute            WSBinding
             class                       ClassWebServiceBindingAttr
             property propConformsTo is  propBasicProfile1_1 of
enumWSIProfiles

             custom-attribute            WebMethod
             class                       ClassWebMethodAttribute.

         repository.
          class ClassFacade                as
"CoolThings.OOCobolAndFlex.Facade"
          class SystemXmlDocument          as "System.Xml.XmlDocument"
          class ApplicationException       as
"System.ApplicationException"
          class SystemString               as "System.String"

          class ClassWebMethodAttribute    as
"System.Web.Services.WebMethodAttribute"
          class ClassWebService            as
"System.Web.Services.WebService"
          class ClassWebServiceAttribute   as
"System.Web.Services.WebServiceAttribute"
          class ClassWebServiceBindingAttr as
"System.Web.Services.WebServiceBindingAttribute"

          enum enumWSIProfiles             as
"System.Web.Services.WsiProfiles"

          property propBasicProfile1_1     as "BasicProfile1_1"
          property propConformsTo          as "ConformsTo"
          property propNamespace           as "Namespace"
          property InnerXML                as "InnerXml"
          property ExceptionMessage        as "Message".

object.
  procedure division.
      method-id. NEW.

      end method NEW.

       method-id. GetContratado as "GetContratado" custom-attribute
WebMethod.
          data division.
              working-storage section.

              01 appException  usage OBJECT REFERENCE
ApplicationException.
              01 facade        USAGE OBJECT REFERENCE ClassFacade.

              linkage section.
              01 inCodigo      usage binary-double signed.
              01 outContratado usage object reference
SystemXmlDocument.

          procedure division using inCodigo returning outContratado.

              invoke ClassFacade "NEW" returning facade

              try
                  invoke facade "GetContratado" using inCodigo
                                       returning outContratado

              catch appException
                  invoke SystemXmlDocument "NEW" returning
outContratado

                  set  InnerXML of outContratado
                       to SystemString::"Concat"("<Error><Message>",
                                         ExceptionMessage of
appException,
                                         "</Message></Error>")
              end-try

              exit method.

      end method GetContratado.
end object.
END CLASS OOCobol.

To implement those features in C# or Java or C++ it is not the answer.
JNI architecture IS a mess, and make maintenance cost go up like a
rocket. Import/export of files is a bad joke, message is NOT MADE for
real time apps, so whenever you mix technologies (Cobol+something),
and you don't delimit the boundaries correctly projects get
jeopardized.

I'm tired to see people who never coded a single line in Cobol (not
you, of course) saying: "Cobol cannot do this, lets do this using C +
Java + messaging blah, blah, blah". This is stupid. I know a lot of
cases where projects like this failed miserably, and even when things
works nobody really knows why, just pray to stay working until they
could move everything into a new environment (NOT). Cobol can and does
design patterns, Webservices, XML, graphics and lot of nice things.
Cobol is good for everything? NO! But even Java has failed in GUI
despite all investment made by Sun and its partners(I know this
better, I'm working to port JSP/Servlets into Flex in my current
project, only JEE classes will be kept), for everything else let do
this correctly (or do it in Cobol or rewrite the entire thing, but
keep your IT environment simple).

I'm suggesting less coding in order to improve productivity, that's
all.

There are a lot of things that I do in C#, Java, TCL, and even in
Perl, but Cobol is my real passion, and I want to see Cobol evolving.
This kind of resistence remind me those guys that tried to stop the
ANS commite to release Cobol-85...This is what really hurts Cobol, not
new (and soon dead) languages.

Regards, Emerson
C# MCP
Sun Java Certified
Vignette V/5 with TCL Certified

Visit my C# open source project (www.redrails.net).

On 2009-09-30 22:11:35 -0500, Emerson <emersonlopes@gmail.com> said:

> Wow, so many twisted mouths and no love at all.
> 
> Pete/Riplin
> 
> There will be no "Cobol community" as you know in ten years from now.

Yes, and they said the mainframe would be dead in 1994. A silly assertation,
as an IBM mainframe today represents the absolute best technology you can
find. That is more and more the reason that mainframes are not only alive and
well more than 15 years after they were supposed to be totally dead, 
but flourishing.

COBOL is like that. It will be around for a long long time to come. Even if the
opportunities in it are shrinking drastically.

Even if some of the COBOL vendors are unbelievably ridiculous in their greed.

And even though IBM keeps trying to kill COBOL (and Assembler), at least once
with every batch of young know-it-alls that arrive at IBM, fresh with 
ideas of how
to completely change the world.

Even if Pete is essentially right in a lot of his views about COBOL vs. 
Microsoft. <grin>

COBOL is not going to go away.


> A new generation, whether you like it or not will take the helm and
> keep current Cobol applications running because THERE IS NO MONEY to
…[7 more quoted lines elided]…
> stuff):

Now you are into the core of the matter - COBOL is simply not designed for
quick and dirty programming. Generations of programmers have been taught
structured design and coding, and the more structure that is imposed on 
anything,
the less flexible that thing becomes. Including computer languages like COBOL.

A good example of a train wreck in language design is C++. Some ideas are
implemented with too much structure, and other ideas not implemented with
enough structure. (Look at exception handling for an example.)  Projects
produced with C+ are often labyrinthine, often fail, and usually have more than
their fair share of  "bugs."

A good example of a highly structured language that is successful is 
Ada. It is not as
flexible as one would like because of that structure, and therefor has 
enjoyed limited
usage in commercial projects. But where it it used, the projects are 
usually quite
successful, and the products produced remarkably free of "bugs."

COBOL projects fall somewhere in between, with much higher success 
rates than C++,
though with more defects than an Ada based project.

Perhaps the answer is to use other technologies when the projects calls 
for them. Extensions of
COBOL into OO programming often are too complex and too difficult to 
understand. Which is what
I intended to point out, though perhaps I  did not make that clear enough.

Why not concentrate on what COBOL does best, and enhance that?  
Everyone will have their
own opinion on what COBOL does the best of course, but I think we can 
safely say that COBOL
has to be stretched all out of shape to drive a highly interactive web 
service. But the same is
true in some ways of C# - it has to be stretched all our of shape to 
deal with transactions. Which is
why it doesn't really - rather it delegates transaction handling to a 
database. Compare that to CICS;
and remember, COBOL speaks CICS very fluently. :)

…[374 more quoted lines elided]…
>> - Show quoted text -

<a id="t-0a4e1771c8"></a>
## Thread: z390 and zcobol full release v1.5.01 with updated test results — 1 msgs

### z390 and zcobol full release v1.5.01 with updated test results

- **From:** "don@higgins.net" <don@higgins.net>
- **Date:** 2009-09-16T04:17:00-07:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<abfcb460-b348-41be-9114-55dd680d5313@e18g2000vbe.googlegroups.com>`

```
z390 and zcobol full release v1.5.01 is now available for download via
www.z390.org.  Note the download links point to www.z390.org for now
as the sourceforge.net site was unavailable for uploading all the
files.  For details on fixes and enhancements in this release visit:

http://www.z390.org/z390_Download_Archive.htm

Both z390 and zcobol are included in the z390 download and install for
Windows and Linux.  For z390 documentation on how to assemble, link,
and execute HLASM compatible assembler programs visit www.z390.org.
For zcobol documentation on how to compile, link, and execute COBOL
programs visit www.zcobol.org.  The only requirement for this open
source software is J2SE 6.0+.  This full release v1.5.01 has been
regression tested on J2SE 1.6.0 update 16 and has been tested with
Windows Vista and XP.  Interactive debugging of the Java source was
done using Eclipse 3.5/  Updated demo and regression test programs are
included in this release.

The major enhancements in this release include:

1.      The open source zcobol compiler now assembles 408 of the NIST
COBOL 1985 test suite programs with no hard assembler errors and just
level 8 MNOTE messages for those functions not yet fully  supported.
zcobol now supports all 9 floating point types plus up to 39 digit
integers using quad word data type in COMPUTE, MOVE, DISPLAY, and
other arithmetic verbs.  zcobol also includes 3 demo programs and 28
regression test programs which can all be compiled and executed.
2.      zCICS version 8 contributed by Melvyn Maltz with additional
COBOL and assembler EXEC CICS support plus reformatted PDF
documentation format contributed by Walter Petras:
a.      EXEC CICS ASSIGN
b.      EXEC CICS INQUIRE FILE
c.       Enhancements to CEMT I FILE, cursor select filename for an
expanded display
d.      This release includes 13 COBOL transactions you can compile
and execute
3.      New CODEPAGE option has been added to support ASCII and EBCDIC
Unicode Charset codepages.  The option has 3 parameters separated by +
including name of ascii codepage, name of EBCDIC code page, and list
option.  The default value is CODEPAGE(ISO-8859-1+IBM1047) which is
compatible with z/OS.  If the third +LIST option is added, a map of
the 2 selected codepages, a dump of the resulting ASCII/EBCDIC
translation tables, and a list of the 64 valid ASCII and 15 valid
EBCDIC Charset codepages available out of the over 162 total Charset
codepages available on J2SE. To suppress the CODEPAGE option and
revert to prior z390 hardcoded ASCII/EBCDIC tables, use NOCODEPAGE
option.
4.      Add ZPAR structured conditional macro assembler based
utilities documented on www.zpar.org:
a.      ZPARGEN – generate batch execution commands for one or more
programs
b.      ZPARERR – summarize the ERR logs for one or more programs.
c.       ZPARMLC – frequency distribution of opcodes for one or more
MLC or BAL source files.
d.      ZPARSUM1 – summarize ERR log braking on first 2 characters of
program name.
e.       ZPARSUM2 – summarize translation, assembly, and execution of
NIST test programs by ID.
f.       ZPARTRS – trace execution showing source assembler lines with
data labels etc.  This can now be used to trace source code execution
of server using zpar\ZPARTRS cics\Z390CICS and to trace local clients
using zpar\ZPARTRS cics\Z390KCP (requires turning on client trace and
renaming local terminal tre file to Z390KCP.TRE)
g.      FIXCRLF – utility to add CR, LF to source (some editors don’t
require CR)
5.      New open source barcode utility in linklib\barcode contributed
by Roger Williams with ABA (www.accessaba.com).
6.      Linklib\FPCONVRT.MAC mainframe compatible floating point
conversion routines contributed by David Bond with Tachyon
(www.tachyonsoft.com) updated to use DFP instructions at ARCHLVL 6.
7.      Upgrade to both the az390 assembler and zcobol to support EXEC
CICS to support a total of 30 DFHRESP and 25 DFHVALUE literals.  Also
add option EDF for use by zCICS.
8.      Issue error message for explicit DROP when the register is not
currently assigned.
9.      Issue az390 warning when identical overlapping ordinary USING
ranges result in selecting higher register.
10.  Add EXEC and LIST macro forms for OPEN, CLOSE, and SNAP macro.
11.  Add support for instructions PFPO, ECTG, and CSST.
12.  Add limited access register support including CPYA, EAR, and SAR
instructions.
13.  Add support for ESTA option 2 PSW.
14.  Add AINSERT support.
15.  Improve literal error handling to clearly identify first source
line reference.

The major fixes in this release include:

1.      Only resolve V(con) to A(con) if local symbol is a CSECT,
otherwise local symbol is unrelated to external symbol by the same
name.
2.      Reset linker RLD count after each NAME command in LKD command
file to prevent erroneous RLD’s being added to following load modules.
3.      Correct some 64 bit shift and floating point conversion
instruction bugs found during debugging of new zcobol support for all
9 floating point types (see RPI 1015 for specifics).
4.      Correct GUAM TN3270 support to return all protected fields
with the modified data bit set on.
5.      Correct KSDS POINT error on single record file.
6.      Correct error handling for ZSTRMAC structured conditional
macro code to detect and report missing label errors.
7.      Correct mz390 to report error 11 invalid continuation on ERR
log.  Previously the error only appeared on BAL file plus error
totals.
8.      Correct error checking for SS type instruction with explicit
offset(length,register) where length is greater than 256 previously
resulting in object code generation error caught by linker.
9.      Correct OPEN and CLOSE macros to only assume register notation
if operand is in (..).
10.  Correct MODCB to use OI/NI versus MVI and support AREALLEN.
11.  Correct ABEND dump processing to prevent multiple threads from
interlacing dumps.
12.  Correct mz390 macro processor to trap any exceptions, report
error, and close all files.
13.  Patch for Linux to support the batch command J2SEOPTIONS
parameter.

For the current pending fixes and enhancements visit:

http://www.z390.org/z390_Support_Request_Log.htm

For documentation on all z390 options including new ALIGN and
CODEPAGE, see:

http://www.z390.org/z390_Options.htm

There is a known outstanding priority 1 issues with this release to be
include in first PTF.  RPI 1083 will correct AINSERT issue with
complex application using nested macros and AINSERT copy statements
not tested with current rt\test\TESTAIN1.MLC and rt\test\TESTAOMS2.MLC
regression tests.

Many thanks to developers Melvyn Maltz, David Bond, Roger Williams,
Abe Kornelis and all the users who have contributed to this release.
The next release of zcobol will have additional functionality
including QSAM and VSAM file I/O in addition to the current LINE
SEQENTIAL (see zcobol\demo\COPYFILE.CBL) support.  Note this COBOL
file support is already available in EXEC CICS COBOL programs.

All feedback, suggestions, and requests for additional enhancements
and fixes are always welcome.

Don Higgins
Don@Higgins.net
www.Don-Higgins.net
```

---

## Thread: WRITE ADVANCING — 26 msgs

### WRITE ADVANCING

- **From:** "William M. Klein" <wmklein@nospam.ix.netcom.com>
- **Date:** 2009-09-17T05:56:33-05:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<EBosm.28421$GS3.19497@en-nntp-07.dc1.easynews.com>`

```
OK,
  Let's go back to COBOL and the days of "line printers" or their equivalent <G>

This is a follow-up on ongoing thread in the OC forum.

There is a question about what happens (should happen) in the case of a program 
that combines WRITER AFTER ADVANCING with WRITE BEFORE ADVANCING to the same 
file.

I thought that there used to be some warnings about this, i.e. that "results may 
be unpredictable or at least undesirable" if you mixed these two.  However, I 
can't find any. (Standard or user documentation)

Does anyone know of any "official" warnings about this?

I may be thinking of combining the (old) IBM extension "WRITE AFTER POSITIONING" 
with "WRITE AFTER ADVANCING" - but I don't know.
```

#### ↳ Re: WRITE ADVANCING

- **From:** docdwarf@panix.com ()
- **Date:** 2009-09-17T13:31:08+00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<h8tdms$lcf$1@reader1.panix.com>`

with defining the first character of a print file (DCB=FBA, etc) and 
specifically addressing it with one of the arcane control-codes because 
the programmer did not want to deal with SPECIAL-NAMES.

the WRITE AFTER POSITIONING statement was not supported under VS COBOL 
II... but that was only twenty or so years ago so it might be called 
'moderately recent'.

###### ↳ ↳ ↳ Re: WRITE ADVANCING

- **From:** SkippyPB <swiegand@Nospam.neo.rr.com>
- **Date:** 2009-09-17T11:38:40-04:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<s7l4b5lh3a56ejhe1m7tmaigvqdncqmg7v@4ax.com>`
- **References:** `<EBosm.28421$GS3.19497@en-nntp-07.dc1.easynews.com> <h8tdms$lcf$1@reader1.panix.com> <rci4b556svl020dh37qeqjjkse225nu2so@4ax.com>`

```
On Thu, 17 Sep 2009 08:38:02 -0600, Howard Brazee <howard@brazee.net>
wrote:

>On Thu, 17 Sep 2009 13:31:08 +0000 (UTC), docdwarf@panix.com () wrote:
>
…[6 more quoted lines elided]…
>placed in the printers for various forms.

My memory says it was used to skip either a number of lines or to a
particular channel.  For example, if you said WRITE PRINT-REC AFTER
POSITIONING 0 , it would double space.  If you said ....AFTER
POSITIONING +, it would suppress spacing.  If 1 through 9 were used,
it would skip to channel 1 through 9 respectively.  Or if you used A,
B or C, it would skip to channel 10, 11, or 12 respectively.

However, if you add the word LINES after the integers (0, 1, 2, 3)
you'd get an eject, single space, double space, triple space
respectively.

Furthermore, if you were writing to an IBM 1442 and said .....AFTER
POSITIONING V (or W), it would select pocket 1 (or 2).

Regards,
```

##### ↳ ↳ Re: WRITE ADVANCING

- **From:** Charlie <foxgrove@shaw.ca>
- **Date:** 2009-09-17T12:19:01-07:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<e9950f8d-bcc2-4181-8664-2af0c957f558@i4g2000prm.googlegroups.com>`
- **References:** `<EBosm.28421$GS3.19497@en-nntp-07.dc1.easynews.com> <h8tdms$lcf$1@reader1.panix.com>`

```
[SNIP]
>
> I do not recall ever using WRITE BEFORE ADVANCING... the only grounds for
…[4 more quoted lines elided]…
>

Back in the day... Honeywell 120....  We always tried to use BEFORE
ADVANCING and avoided AFTER ADVANCING.  Printing was directly to the
printer.  With BEFORE your line would print during one rotation of the
print drum and then the paper would feed.  Control returned to your
program while the paper was moving.  With AFTER the paper would move,
then the line would print with control returned to you program after
the line started printing.  Paper movement was relatively slow,
compared to a single drum rotation.  Using BEFORE was much quicker as
your program could proceed while the paper was moving.
```

Shucks... t'warn't nothin'.  A page I find *really* useful is 
http://publib.boulder.ibm.com/cgi-bin/bookmgr/LIBRARY .

>
>I was amazed at all the differences between OS/VS COBOL and VS COBOL II, 
>and that most of them were features I never used or situations I never 
>encountered.  I certainly was not aware of them at the time.  How did we

I'm not sure about 'we'... but many places I worked (usual caveat about 
'sick shops' applies) ignored it.  They ran OS/VS COBOL as much as they 
could and when they Absolutely Had To their 'conversion strategy' 
consisted of 'programs that need compiling will now use IGYCRCTL, anything 
else will remain untouched'...

... until they started to run into conflicts between the lower-level 
subroutines (ILB0 vs IGZY) and programs that had been running just 
fine for years began blowing up with S0C4s on READs.

From what I saw... places really didn't make serious efforts to shift away 
from OLDBOL until Y2K remediation began.

DD

###### ↳ ↳ ↳ Re: WRITE ADVANCING

_(thread depth: 5)_

- **From:** bo774@FreeNet.Carleton.CA (Kelly Bert Manning)
- **Date:** 2009-09-26T23:04:05+00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<h9m6l5$e79$1@theodyn.ncf.ca>`
- **References:** `<EBosm.28421$GS3.19497@en-nntp-07.dc1.easynews.com> <h8tefk$ous$1@news.eternal-september.org> <h8tgnl$qm0$1@reader1.panix.com> <GStsm.180386$O23.92961@newsfe11.iad> <h8tqlu$rmq$1@reader1.panix.com>`

```
 (docdwarf@panix.com) writes:
> In article <GStsm.180386$O23.92961@newsfe11.iad>, tlmfru <lacey@mts.net> wrote:
>>Oooooh, Doc.  "AFTER BEFORE ADVANCING"!
…[38 more quoted lines elided]…
> DD

But the BEFORE text will overwrite the line of AFTER text, even
if MIXING BEFORE and AFTER works "as expected".

That may be what the programmer intended, but would a different
person maintaining the code spot that immediately?

Some vendors seem set against mixing and matching. I'd call it bad
style, but expect it to work. I haven't seen a Honeywell compiler
since 1980, but I do recall that HIS GCOS 4js had a 100% overhead
for WRITE AFTER. I'd always write long reports to disk or tape so
that they could be reprinted if the printer mangled them or of a
page got lost in the mail. I found long HIS COBOL 74 reports took
up twice as much space and printed slowly. Browsing the files
revealed that it generated pairs of print records for WRITE AFTER.
The first record would have the requested paper movement command
followed by a second reord with a null slew and the text data. The
impact printer speed seemed noticeably slower than WRITE BEFORE
output.

When we converted from HIS COBOL 74 to IBM's COBOL 68 some folks
spent a lot of time convering WRITE BEFORE to WRITE AFTER. My
recollection is that if your print files were FBM or VBM
there wasn't much difference. IBM had Machine Control Codes
for both BEFORE and AFTER.

I led the migration to VS COBOL II at our data center in the late
1980s, and don't recall any issue with either BEFORE or AFTER
not being supported. There were enough of both that I would
have expected it to come up. We did leave it till late, perhaps
it was an issue with earlier releases of VS COBOL II.

How common is/was WRITE BEFORE? With impact printers in the 1980s
our site had programmers go to what seem like a lot of trouble
to code a few programs to print then slew, squeezing  a few %
faster speed out of the line printers for particularly long 
reports. In general it seemed more complex to code the programs
for doing that.
```

```
In article <aNOsm.129375$nL7.115746@newsfe18.iad>,
tlmfru <lacey@mts.net> wrote:

[snip]

>I should add that after reflecting, I remember that I wrote one program
>using "before" exclusively, just to annoy a programmer on the staff who
>positively broke out in warts if anyone used an "inefficient" method, of
>anything.  He went berserk!   It was a weekly program that produced one page
>of output so it really didn't matter.  Oooh that was fun.

Leaving aside the all-too-human enjoyment of occaisionally inflicting bits 
of petty sadism on Those Who Really Deserve It... this caused me to think 
about two things:

1) If Mr Efficiency was so concerned maybe it was time to compile with a 
PMAP and ask to see where additional costs were being incurred, calculate 
these costs per run and then compare those costs to the costs of 
re-coding, re-testing and implementing to Prod something more efficient.  
(As you mentioned, a weekly job with one page of output)

2) I was taught that - in most cases, there are exceptions to every rule, 
including this one - that writing a report to disk and then printing the 
dataset with a utility (eg, IEBGENER) would, in the long run, prove to be 
cheaper than re-running the report when delivery-clerk misdirected a copy 
or a Corner-Office Idiot lost it and blithely ordered 'Oh, just re-run the 
job'... ESPECIALLY when it was a job that updated things.

DD
```

- **Message-ID:** `<h8tv1m$1lm3$1@si05.rsvl.unisys.com>`

```
"William M. Klein" <wmklein@nospam.ix.netcom.com> wrote in message 
news:EBosm.28421$GS3.19497@en-nntp-07.dc1.easynews.com...
> There is a question about what happens (should happen) in the case of a 
> program that combines WRITER AFTER ADVANCING with WRITE BEFORE ADVANCING 
> to the same file.

With the Unisys MCP COBOL74 and COBOL85 compilers,
WRITE AFTER ADVANCING and WRITE BEFORE ADVANCING are both allowed 
separately.
Mixing BEFORE and AFTER in the same WRITE statement is not allowed.

Damian Thomas
(I do not speak for my employer.  These are my opinions only.)
```

#### ↳ Re: WRITE ADVANCING

- **From:** "Vince Coen" <VBCoenDespawn@btconnect.com>
- **Date:** 2009-09-19T14:43:04
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<1253367784@f1.n250.z2.fidonet.ftn>`
- **References:** `<EBosm.28421$GS3.19497@en-nntp-07.dc1.easynews.com>`

```
Hello William!

17 Sep 09 11:56, William M. Klein wrote to All:

 WMK> There is a question about what happens (should happen) in the case of
 WMK> a program that combines WRITER AFTER ADVANCING with WRITE BEFORE
 WMK> ADVANCING to the same file.

In a stack of program/modules rewritten for OC I have both during production 
of the page headings depending if it is page one i.e., issuing a write 
printline after page will waste one sheet of paper despite it being at topo of 
form when using a laser or inkjet type printer. So I issue write before's on 
page one and replace 'before page' with 'before 1' during the first 2 lines of 
the headings. line 3 to whatever then reverts to standad eg write after having 
printed a blank line to sync up the two styles.

This works well, as one would expect.  You might well be referring to 
'positioning' for which I do not recall using let alone having problems with 
but there again I don't remember too much of the early 60's and Cobol 
programming.

Its hard enough going from one room to another and trying to remember why :)

[And that is not so much a joke]

Vince
```

<a id="t-623bb6eb4f"></a>
## Thread: OT: decline of the print industry — 1 msgs

_Topics: [`Off-topic and spam`](topics.md#spam)_

### OT: decline of the print industry

- **From:** "tlmfru" <lacey@mts.net>
- **Date:** 2009-09-19T19:50:01-05:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<R_etm.436300$Ta5.371415@newsfe15.iad>`

```
Robert Wagner - wherever he is - made some comments on this subject which I
disagreed with, but I have an example of what he may have been talking
about.  It's "E-Week", Sept. 7/09.  It's "34" pages long but that's
misleading, because page 1 & 2 are the outside & inside front covers.  Of
the remaining "32", 12 are full-page ads; 3 are the table of contents.  Of
the "17" left, just 8 are full-page articles.  The major part of the
contents is devoted to Windows Server 2008 R2, MS System Center Virtual
Machines Manager, and Windows 7.  How are the mighty fallen!  E-Week used to
be 70 or 80 pages, with several columnists, content from all over the I/T
universe, and always enough variety to keep up the interest.  I'd say that
this publication doesn't have too long remaining in print in this world.
And it isn't the only one.  I used to have subscriptions to "Computerworld
Canada" and "Computing Canada" and "Infosystems Canada" - all free, all of
wide interest.  Now "I-C" is long gone, "CwC" and "CC" have merged and the
result is much skinnier than either one before was; and it's bi-monthly.  At
least it's still free.

Some of the non-IT magazines to which I subscribe - and all of which I pay
for - are doing well and even expanding.  I wonder if there's a pattern
here?

Good night, Mrs. Calabash - wherever you are.  J.D.


PL
```

---

<a id="t-7f54a108c0"></a>
## Thread: Happy Birthday — 5 msgs

### Happy Birthday

- **From:** "HeyBub" <heybub@NOSPAMgmail.com>
- **Date:** 2009-09-20T18:25:11-05:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<af2dnc1rsod-JCvXnZ2dnUVZ_jGdnZ2d@earthlink.com>`

```
"In May 1959, during a meeting at the Pentagon in Washington, D.C., the US 
Department of Defense organized a committee charged with developing a "short 
range" approach to a common business computing language. And on September 
18th of that year, the new Short Range Committee coined the name COBOL, 
short for Common Business-Oriented Language."

http://www.theregister.co.uk/2009/09/18/cobol_name_birthday/

Only 15 years to retirement.
```

#### ↳ Re: Happy Birthday

- **From:** Rene_Surop <infodynamics_ph@yahoo.com>
- **Date:** 2009-09-21T18:27:07-07:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<137603b8-442e-4e7f-b9ea-ea7075f12055@a39g2000pre.googlegroups.com>`
- **References:** `<af2dnc1rsod-JCvXnZ2dnUVZ_jGdnZ2d@earthlink.com>`

```
A kind of news that never stop to amaze me how Cobol evolves.

Though I don't have an experience yet on the declining Cobol trend in
my area, it seems that Pete Dashwood comments makes me wanted to shift
if not associate my Cobol codes to other technologies. From day one
Pete suggestions for migration popup into mind, the main reason why
people wanted change is because of COSTING. It is not;
a.  Cobol programmers are declining (this is a myth because Cobol
language is easy to learn and new breed of Cobol programmers are even
growing, and most of them are coming from a desktop-based environment
who knows .NET)
b.  lack of functionality (this is even more a argument in disguise.
Cobol language is 'basically' created for business functionalities and
not API-based programming. Most developers tend to associate business
programming logic to systems programming and this is not supposed to
be. In fact, ALL that I need in business data computing is in Cobol
language already. Re-inventing the wheel is not an advice.)

If Cobol vendor thinks that a functionally matured language is the
advantage AND keep on raising their fees... then eventually they'll
killing the mere existence of it. And with this I will positively
agree with Pete.

I haven't look at PERCobol IDE (with JSPs) product yet but it's worth
a try. Maybe online Cobol product development cost will cut it down if
this product is reasonable.
```

they have a tool that works, it is easy to stick with that tool.

Of course, companies could buy the .NET compilers - but I haven't seen
that this market is sizeable.    I haven't personally seen any
mainframe companies going that way.

I think you're right, Bill.

Smaller compaines simply can't afford to buy stuff they don't need.

Larger companies see it as a tiny percentage of the overall budget and it is 
an "insurance policy" in case they need it.

Unfortunately, there is far too much reliance being placed on what Salesmen 
are saying.

And they are saying whatever sells software, in some cases... (I would 
stress that not all salespeople do this...)

It would be OK, if you could return the goods when you realised you had made 
a mistake but, with software, you can't.

Pete.

## Thread: IMS COBOL Application Development Workshops coming to Germany in October — 1 msgs

_Topics: [`Mainframe, z/OS, JCL, CICS`](topics.md#mainframe)_

### IMS COBOL Application Development Workshops coming to Germany in October

- **From:** "denis.gaebler" <denis.gaebler@googlemail.com>
- **Date:** 2009-09-22T01:49:07-07:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<c6eee173-39c1-453b-9944-b2adf136ba8f@f10g2000vbf.googlegroups.com>`

```
Hi,

posted is the invitation to our free of charge IMS COBOL Application
Development Workshops in Germany in October. The workshops were
prepared by the IMS Silicon Valley Lab and include Hands-on Labs
(Laptops are provided).
The workshops are in english and of course there is the possibility to
chat with Deepak Kohli or Richard Tran about individual IMS questions.
These are one day workshops (including coffee and lunch) which take
place in the following cities:

Monday, October 12th 2009:
Stuttgart, IBM Forum

Tuesday, October 13th 2009:
Düsseldorf, IBM Forum

Wednesday, October 14th 2009:
Frankfurt, IBM Forum

Thursday, October 15th 2009:
München/Munich, IBM Forum

Please register using the following website:
http://www-05.ibm.com/de/events/fromzerotozhero/cobol/
The link also contains the agenda.

We hope to welcome you at one of the dates above.

PS: Please feel free to forward the invitation to interested parties
in your company.

## Thread: OO Cobol nice things — 1 msgs

_Topics: [`Object-oriented COBOL`](topics.md#oo)_

### OO Cobol nice things

- **From:** Emerson <emersonlopes@gmail.com>
- **Date:** 2009-09-22T06:25:15-07:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<f0485772-a101-42c4-a30f-01fff3810058@g23g2000vbr.googlegroups.com>`

```
Hello,

I would like to share with you an example of how to use OO Cobol to
post a Twitter status update. I wrote this using NetCobol.Net 4, but
it is very ease to port to NetExpress).

http://www.twitter.com/100CoolThings

The code can be downloaded from my web site http://www.100coolthings.net

Regards, Emerson
```

<a id="t-f7eef4c838"></a>
## Thread: ��� 20 Things You Might Not Know About COBOL — 30 msgs

### ��� 20 Things You Might Not Know About COBOL

- **From:** Howard Brazee <howard@brazee.net>
- **Date:** 2009-09-22T10:36:21-06:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<e7vhb59sc5e9q0i9lv7cn2j1mf5idt6iii@4ax.com>`

```
http://www.eweek.com/c/a/Enterprise-Applications/20-Things-You-Might-Not-Know-About-COBOL-As-the-Language-Turns-50-103943/?kc=EWKNLITA09222009STR2
```

#### ↳ 20 things Taft doesn't know about COBOL... WAS: 20 Things You Might Not Know About COBOL

- **From:** "Pete Dashwood" <dashwood@removethis.enternet.co.nz>
- **Date:** 2009-09-23T17:51:56+12:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<7htrbkF2v856lU1@mid.individual.net>`
- **References:** `<e7vhb59sc5e9q0i9lv7cn2j1mf5idt6iii@4ax.com>`

```
Howard Brazee wrote:
> http://www.eweek.com/c/a/Enterprise-Applications/20-Things-You-Might-Not-Know-About-COBOL-As-the-Language-Turns-50-103943/?kc=EWKNLITA09222009STR2


Here's 20 things Taft doesn't know about COBOL:

1. 85% of all statistics (without citation) are invented on the spot...
2. There may be 2 million people directly involved in COBOL (mainly in 
India, China, and the sub-continent), but there are 60 million directly 
involved in other languages, across the globe.
3. The COBOL 2002 standard has not been implemented by any major (or minor) 
vendor, in its entirety.
4. The "new" standard he promises for "the early 2010s", should have been 
ready 3 years ago. (5 years between standards is a reasonable and acceptable 
period for most computer languages.)
5. Repeating figures from a very old Gartner report (since "qualified" even 
by Gartner), no matter how much you WANT them to be true, does NOT make them 
so...
6. The procedural paradigm COBOL was developed for, is not relevant to a 
world of networked computing. COBOL has been overtaken by events.
7. BCOOL is one anagram of COBOL; BOLOCs is another...
8. The 5 billion lines of new COBOL every year are being written on a 
handful of Government sites. Places where money is no object and 
modernization is anathema. In fact, they are probably being written by ONE 
government...; no prizes for guessing which.
9. "Mission Critical" does NOT mean "fossilized, serial, procedures which 
require archaic batch processing..." Even if that is what mainframes are 
mostly good at...
10. Some simple arithmetic should have given Taft pause... If his claim 
regarding COBOL processing  more than 200 times the number of GOOGLE 
Searches per day could be true, it would mean the ENTIRE POPULATION of 
Planet Earth (men, women, and children, every single person...) causing a 
COBOL transaction every 7 minutes of the working day.  Given that less than 
30% of the planet's population even have access to a personal or mainframe 
computer, this seems extremely unlikely. Draw your own conclusion.
11. Today "15% of all new applications will be written in COBOL..." So, 85% 
of all new applications will NOT be. Twenty years ago COBOL had 75% of the 
market. Today it's 15%. Hard to see a growth trend there...
12. "70% of all business applications are on a mainframe."  I hope they back 
it up regularly...
13. "COBOL is being re-energized."  Unfortunately the same cannot be said 
for most of its practitioners. They are fading away and failing to be 
replaced.
14. "COBOL has been fashioned for execution within framework environments 
such as Java and .NET."  And as soon as programmers learn those environments 
they abandon COBOL for Java or C#.
15. "There are $2 trillion dollars invested in COBOL..."  And that's just to 
keep it running for one Government... Many businesses have found out they 
simply can't afford the price of labour intensive software maintenance which 
COBOL demands. COBOL maintenance is error prone and expensive. Mainly 
because it is verbose and you therefore need more of it than you do of other 
languages.
16. Anyone seriously investing in a COBOL future in this day and age is 
either myopic or stupid. (Supporting legacy is the ONLY case where you can 
justify continued use of it...) There are MUCH better solutions available 
and they cost much less to implement and maintain. Attachment to COBOL has 
to be on emotional/tradional rather than rational grounds; it cannot be 
justified economically, and even functionally, there is nothing you can do 
in COBOL that can't be done (more cheaply) in another language.
17. "Five billion lines of new COBOL are developed every year." And 4 
billion of those are replacing previous COBOL code that has become 
"unmaintainable"...
18. "Dijkstra once said, "The use of COBOL cripples the mind; its teaching 
should, therefore, be regarded as a criminal offense." " He said it as a 
joke. But he was not far off the mark. It isn't that COBOL "cripples the 
mind" it is more that it "closes the mind". It is a bit like the guitarist 
who consistently played a single chord. When his wife gently asked him why 
he didn't move his fingers around like other guitarists she had seen, he 
replied:"They're looking for the place; I've found it."
19. Modern software is comprised of objects and layers. This approach means 
more easy platform interopability, better functional isolation 
(encapsulation), and easier, quicker, and cheaper maintenance (object 
reuse). This approach evolved out of a search for solutions to the problems 
created when you DON'T use objects and layers. And THAT was largely 
predicated on COBOL legacy.
20. COBOL was a brilliant response to the perceived needs of the 1960s. When 
you had a centralised processor that did everything, based on the Von 
Neumann model of sequential execution. But things have come a long way since 
then. COBOL should be allowed to go with dignity.

Pete.
 -- 
"I used to write COBOL...now I can do anything."
```

##### ↳ ↳ Re: 20 things Taft doesn't know about COBOL... WAS: 20 Things You Might Not Know About COBOL

On Wed, 23 Sep 2009 17:51:56 +1200, "Pete Dashwood"

I was thinking most of the stuff you posted when I read the article.
The main exception is that I don't associate CoBOL so much with
government work.

However I think the following may be a matter of how Taft defined
"transaction".     

>10. Some simple arithmetic should have given Taft pause... If his claim 
>regarding COBOL processing  more than 200 times the number of GOOGLE 
…[4 more quoted lines elided]…
>computer, this seems extremely unlikely. Draw your own conclusion.

silly, but I suspect that may be what this stat did.

###### ↳ ↳ ↳ Re: 20 things Taft doesn't know about COBOL... WAS: 20 Things You Might Not Know About COBOL

- **From:** "Pete Dashwood" <dashwood@removethis.enternet.co.nz>
- **Date:** 2009-09-25T03:43:32+12:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<7i1id2F2v8oeaU1@mid.individual.net>`
- **References:** `<e7vhb59sc5e9q0i9lv7cn2j1mf5idt6iii@4ax.com> <7htrbkF2v856lU1@mid.individual.net> <19umb5hqe82qu5qjqhr1sn1c0koim50k6k@4ax.com>`

```
Howard Brazee wrote:
> On Wed, 23 Sep 2009 17:51:56 +1200, "Pete Dashwood"
> <dashwood@removethis.enternet.co.nz> wrote:
…[18 more quoted lines elided]…
> silly, but I suspect that may be what this stat did.

Very possibly. It would be in in keeping with the general silliness of the 
article. (My response was approriately silly... :-))

I guess, in the light of some private mail I had on this, and your very 
sensible response, Howard, I'd better clear up a few points...:

1. Some of what I wrote here was tongue-in-cheek and not intended to be 
taken seriously.

2. I do NOT honestly believe that the US Government is the last stronghold 
of Fortress COBOL. (Although they probably contribute significantly to the 
claimed 5 billion lines a year...)

3. I am getting really tired of people who keep quoting the bloody Gartner 
figures from over 10 years ago and telling us everything in the garden is 
rosy and there will be a new standard in 2010, and did you know that COBOL 
is Object Oriented now, just like the modern stuff?

4. Yes, I did know. I did know 15 years ago when I received scorn and 
ridicule for suggesting it might be a good approach. After pushing through 
objects into components I received more flak. "OO is a con." "Why would we 
need it?" "It's a fad..." Now the penny drops and people who should know 
better write articles like Taft's as if  that ship is still in the harbour, 
when it is long gone and over the horizon. OO cannot save COBOL. The only 
way that COULD happen would be if there were no other OO languages and COBOL 
was the only game in town. There WAS a time when that was true, but it is 
not this time. (OO CAN ease the transition of existing COBOL into other 
environments...)

5. When anyone over 30 years of age starts using slogans like: "COBOL is an 
anagram of "BCOOL"  it is just sad. It increases in sadness logarithmically, 
with every decade over 30 the person is. Unfortunately this does tend to 
bring out the worst in me.

6. I have sent Taft a copy of my response. (No point in talking behind his 
back; besides, it isn't personal.) I'm not expecting a response...

Pete.
```

```
On Sep 24, 10:46 am, SkippyPB <swieg...@Nospam.neo.rr.com> wrote:
> On Thu, 24 Sep 2009 07:53:04 -0600, Howard Brazee <how...@brazee.net>
> wrote:

FWIW:

There are currently about 400,000 ATMs installed in the United
States.  A figure from about ten years ago was that the average ATM in
the US processed about 6400 transactions per month.  That was with
140,000 ATMs, so the average is likely a fair bit lower now, but still
gives us a ballpark:  The raw rates imply about 85 million ATM
transactions per day in the U.S.  That seems a bit high (it implies
that one transaction every 3.5 days for every person in the US), but
not massively so, perhaps a factor of two or three.

Reports are that about half the worlds ATMs are in the United States,
assuming area's less densely covered by ATMs have higher average
transaction rates per-ATM, we could ballpark about 100m ATM
transactions per day, globally.

Search Engine Watch reports just under 7 billion U.S. Google searches
for August 2009 (out of 10.8 billion total U.S.), or about 230 million
per day.  200 times that rate implies 153 transactions per day per
person in the U.S.

For credit and debit cards, there were about 44 billion transactions
in the U.S. in 2005, or about 120 million per day (which corresponds
well with another figure I have that puts the number of transactions
at about 360/year per household, of which there are about 110
million).

Of course the real question is why one would compare numbers of
financial transactions to numbers of Google searches.
```

- **From:** docdwarf@panix.com ()
- **Date:** 2009-09-25T01:06:00+00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<h9h51o$3ot$1@reader1.panix.com>`
- **References:** `<e7vhb59sc5e9q0i9lv7cn2j1mf5idt6iii@4ax.com> <19umb5hqe82qu5qjqhr1sn1c0koim50k6k@4ax.com> <ct4nb5lrjkekq4e0fk5phfdhmkd9vf2sk0@4ax.com> <f0b9fcdf-3854-41d5-af61-d4bde30b8fbf@d34g2000vbm.googlegroups.com>`

```
In article <f0b9fcdf-3854-41d5-af61-d4bde30b8fbf@d34g2000vbm.googlegroups.com>,
robertwessel2@yahoo.com <robertwessel2@yahoo.com> wrote:

[snip]

>Of course the real question is why one would compare numbers of
>financial transactions to numbers of Google searches.

Really?  Being a bit of the Technical Type I got caught up with the 
definition of 'transaction'; for me it had the same kind of slipperiness 
as LUW... errrrrr, Logical Unit of Work, the signal for a CICS SYNCPOINT, 
for those who understand such things.

A person puts a card in a machine, deposits money, withdraws money, checks 
a balance, receives an NSF or NOAUTH response to a request and walks 
away... this is a transaction, right?  Or...

A card is inserted into the machine.  The machine verifies *at the machine 
interface* that the card's mag strip is valid.  This is a transaction.

The machine, having recognised a valid mag strip, requests a PIN.  This is 
a transaction.

The user hits the keys... assuming that each key is not verified at the 
pressing the user hits 'all done' and the PIN is captured and formatted by 
the machine.  This is a transaction.

The machine sends the PIN to whatever 'source of good PINs' exists (some 
verify against the card, some elsewhere).  This is a transaction.

The verification comes back as 'good' or 'no good'.  This is a 
transaction.

... and so on.  I'm sure I'm missing a few steps here and there but... 
once it gets to the bank level I can think of, for a withdrawal, six 
COBOL transactions used for a single withdrawal:

1) Open/verify the account.
2) Verify the account is not frozen.
3) Verify that subtracting the amount requested will not violate (rules).
4) Send a 'disburse (amount of currency) signal to the ATM.
5) Decrement the amount remaining in the account.
6) Send an 'all done' signal to wherever it is needed.

So... how are 'transactions' being counted, anyhow?

DD
```

```
On Sep 24, 8:06 pm, docdw...@panix.com () wrote:
> In article <f0b9fcdf-3854-41d5-af61-d4bde30b8...@d34g2000vbm.googlegroups.com>,
>
…[43 more quoted lines elided]…
> So... how are 'transactions' being counted, anyhow?


FWIW, many of the ATM transactions actually combine all six of the
steps you listed.  You put in your card, enter the PIN, select your
function, and then the whole thing goes as a single "transaction."
And if you perform several transactions, these each generate a single
"complete" transaction including your account data.  Of course that's
not always true, commonly account verification is done separately, so
often it's *two* "transactions," and then sometimes things get broken
up further.
```

###### ↳ ↳ ↳ Re: 20 things Taft doesn't know about COBOL... WAS: 20 Things You Might Not Know About COBOL

_(thread depth: 7)_

- **From:** docdwarf@panix.com ()
- **Date:** 2009-09-25T17:35:38+00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<h9iv1a$mrn$1@reader1.panix.com>`
- **References:** `<e7vhb59sc5e9q0i9lv7cn2j1mf5idt6iii@4ax.com> <f0b9fcdf-3854-41d5-af61-d4bde30b8fbf@d34g2000vbm.googlegroups.com> <h9h51o$3ot$1@reader1.panix.com> <ef26c028-affe-4a71-9025-87a83791e0d5@e18g2000vbe.googlegroups.com>`

```
In article <ef26c028-affe-4a71-9025-87a83791e0d5@e18g2000vbe.googlegroups.com>,
robertwessel2@yahoo.com <robertwessel2@yahoo.com> wrote:
>On Sep 24, 8:06?pm, docdw...@panix.com () wrote:
>> In article
…[16 more quoted lines elided]…
>> away... this is a transaction, right? ?Or...

[snip]

>> ... and so on. ?I'm sure I'm missing a few steps here and there but...
>> once it gets to the bank level I can think of, for a withdrawal, six
…[14 more quoted lines elided]…
>function, and then the whole thing goes as a single "transaction."

There's the rub, Mr Wessel, and hence my musings.  According to one 
definition ( http://www.merriam-webster.com/dictionary/transaction ), 2b, 
a transaction is 'a communicative action or activity involving two parties 
or things that reciprocally affect or influence each other.'

The COBOL system takes the account number transmitted from the ATM and 
attempts to open/verify the account associated with this number.  If the 
account exists things continue, if it doesn't (or is marked as 'don't 
allow activities against this account') then the COBOL system generates an 
'out of luck, Charlie' message, sends it back to the ATM and the card is 
returned (or, in some cases, kept).

This is a single communicative action (from the ATM to the Big Iron), 
involving two parties (ATM/Big Iron) that reciprocally affects or 
influences each other (the Big Iron does other stuff and the ATM keeps the 
card or the Big Iron says 'no go' and it stops there.  By that definition 
this is 'a transaction'... and, as you note, it may be perceived by the 
participants as a part of the transaction of a successful or failing 
banking activity.

My point was that 'just because it can be seen as one interaction does not 
require that only one step is performed'... and by the use of the 
indefinite article singular ('*a* communicative action or activity') it 
meets the criteria of the definition of 'a transaction'.

To take it out of the World of Computers... 'she got herself a loaf of 
bread' might be called 'a transaction'... but it might be more accurately 
seen as an activity; she picked up her car keys (affecting the status of 
her immediate possessions and the position of the keys), she left the 
house (affecting the number of people in the house and out of it), she got 
into her car (likewise as previous), she started her car (affecting the 
status of the engine's condition and the vehicle's ability to move)...

... or, as the French say, und so weiter.  In answer to Interview Question 
Number 287: 'What constitutes a Logical Unit of Work?' my response has 
always been 'the completion of steps which satisfy the shop standards for 
issuing a SYNCPOINT'.

>And if you perform several transactions, these each generate a single
>"complete" transaction including your account data.  Of course that's
>not always true, commonly account verification is done separately, so
>often it's *two* "transactions," and then sometimes things get broken
>up further.

There's the rub o'er which I muse... what are the criteria for this 
'breaking up'?

DD
```

###### ↳ ↳ ↳ Re: 20 things Taft doesn't know about COBOL... WAS: 20 Things You Might Not Know About COBOL

_(thread depth: 6)_

- **From:** "Frank Swarbrick" <Frank.Swarbrick@efirstbank.com>
- **Date:** 2009-09-29T17:39:26-06:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<4AC2464E.6F0F.0085.0@efirstbank.com>`
- **References:** `<e7vhb59sc5e9q0i9lv7cn2j1mf5idt6iii@4ax.com> <19umb5hqe82qu5qjqhr1sn1c0koim50k6k@4ax.com> <ct4nb5lrjkekq4e0fk5phfdhmkd9vf2sk0@4ax.com> <f0b9fcdf-3854-41d5-af61-d4bde30b8fbf@d34g2000vbm.googlegroups.com> <h9h51o$3ot$1@reader1.panix.com>`

```
For what it's worth (nothing), here is how the ATMs that I work with on a
daily basis function...

From the time you enter your card until the time you complete entering your
request information (PIN, function, amount, etc.) there is no "external"
interaction until after that final keypress where the terminal goes in to
it's "please wait" state.  At that time all of the information, including
the magnetic stripe data and the PIN, is gathered together into a single
request message that is sent to the host system that the ATM is connected
to.  The host forwards the request to wherever it needs to go to be
authorized.  When that response is received it is passed back to the ATM. 
Then ATM then sends a "confirmation" back to the host once the money is
dispensed.  That is the end of a "normal" ATM transaction.  

Now of course the ATM does a lot of things interally every time you press a
key.  I have no idea if anything on the ATM itself is written in Cobol,
though my guess is it is not.

Anyway, I wouldn't consider those six steps you refer to as distinct
transactions.  But that's just me.

Interestingly (to me, anyway!) much of the above changes in the "GUI ATM"
world.  We don't have any of these machines, but apparently they do some
"server interaction" as you press various buttons.  For instance, from what
I recall when we were looking in to going this direction, when you enter (or
swipe) your card the ATM does indeed query a server, specifying your card
information.  This allows the ATM to customize your session based on
personal information stored at the host.  It may even be possible for it to
greet you by name, though I have never seen this.
```

```

>Anyway, I wouldn't consider those six steps you refer to as distinct
>transactions.  But that's just me.

[snip]

>> ... and so on.  I'm sure I'm missing a few steps here and there but... 
>> once it gets to the bank level I can think of, for a withdrawal, six 
…[10 more quoted lines elided]…
>> So... how are 'transactions' being counted, anyhow?

If your disagreement is with 'distinction' then it seems, Mr Swarbrick, 
that it is one you created... I didn't use that word.  Just for laffs, 
though, and so that more might be learned... what are your reason(s) for 
not considering these activities to be transactions?

DD

Well I don't want to get into a numbers war but I'm currently involved

had 6.25 million ATM transactions.  So I think your 6400 a month
figure even from 10 years ago doesn't paint a very accurate picture of
what goes on today.

It always confused me... I've consulted with a few banks of some size, 
here and there, and they always seem to know where every penny comes from, 
where it goes and how it gets accounted for every step of the way...

stock response is 'Oh, we don't really have a way to calculate/segregrate 
them.'

I figure that if it can show up as a line item on my statement there must 
be *some* way to address it as a particular kind of transaction... but 
what do I know, I'se jes' a COBOL-codin' fool.

>In article <4desb5ha41jiqjuf4scuf8naml6krrmt91@4ax.com>,
>SkippyPB  <swiegand@Nospam.neo.rr.com> wrote:
…[25 more quoted lines elided]…
>DD

Depending on what system the banks are using they may not know where
their input comes from.  But the system I support does know and, by
bank option, can charge per transaction if they wish.  Some of the
"foreign ATM" stuff is actually done by the ATM software or third
party servicer and passed to the bank.  More and more banks are using
third party servicers to handle all of their ATM and POS traffic and
just passing the debit and or credit and or fee back to the host
mainframe.

Regards,
```
