```
On Sep 25, 10:30 am, SkippyPB <swieg...@Nospam.neo.rr.com> wrote:
> On Thu, 24 Sep 2009 16:21:30 -0700 (PDT), "robertwess...@yahoo.com"
>
…[37 more quoted lines elided]…
> what goes on today.


It can't be all that far off.  That's one transaction every 6.75
minutes over the entire month.  Most ATMs are likely to show much
heavier uses during parts of the day, and be almost idle at others.
Nor are all ATM heavily used - while some will have near continuous
usage during the day, others, such as those in convenience stores,
clearly have much lighter usage.

As mentioned elsewhere, it does depend on what's being counted - if a
single ATM "transaction" from the customer's point of view generates a
dozen "transactions" from a data processing point of view...

What's the transaction rate per customer for this bank?  That might
tell us something.
```

```
> end up being processed on a mainframe by COBOL.

So we are led to believe by people like Taft.

Who actually knows?

I bank with a bank that dropped their mainframe systems several years ago. 
They still process a large number of ATM transactions every day, as well as 
other work.


 What about POS
> terminals?  People don't need access to a personal computer or a
> mainframe to enact a transaction that gets processed by COBOL.

If you assume that COBOL processes the majority of them.

need to do about it, serious harm can be done.

"Don't worry, everything's fine, COBOL has a bright future"  while people

by other things.

A young person reading Taft's article might be encouraged to spend time, 
energy, and money in learning and practicing a skill that has no future.

I don't know about you, but when I was young, I never had much money, and 
what I had needed to be directed to the acquirement of skills that had a 
chance of paying off.

I said my piece; thank God for Usenet :-).

Pete.
```

###### ↳ ↳ ↳ Re: 20 things Taft doesn't know about COBOL... WAS: 20 Things You Might Not Know About COBOL

_(thread depth: 6)_

- **From:** "Pete Dashwood" <dashwood@removethis.enternet.co.nz>
- **Date:** 2009-09-25T22:08:48+12:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<7i3j5eF2v454eU1@mid.individual.net>`
- **References:** `<e7vhb59sc5e9q0i9lv7cn2j1mf5idt6iii@4ax.com> <19umb5hqe82qu5qjqhr1sn1c0koim50k6k@4ax.com> <ct4nb5lrjkekq4e0fk5phfdhmkd9vf2sk0@4ax.com> <7i2h9eF2vlqd6U1@mid.individual.net> <h9h5du$3ot$2@reader1.panix.com>`

```
docdwarf@panix.com wrote:
> In article <7i2h9eF2vlqd6U1@mid.individual.net>,
> Pete Dashwood <dashwood@removethis.enternet.co.nz> wrote:
…[12 more quoted lines elided]…
> DD

Exactly.

40 years ago, COBOL was in that category. No question that if you wanted a 
career in commercial computer programming, you were going to need it, just 
as you needed to have experience on IBM hardware.

My contention is that that is no longer the case and people need to acquire 
other skills in other areas. In fact, the MAJORITY of people who program 
computers for a living today DON'T need COBOL OR IBM mainframe experience.

And there is even an argument that having it can be counter productive. (I 
know of two contract programmers who removed their COBOL experience from 
their CVs because it seemed to hinder them getting jobs. I was NOT one of 
them; I've always been proud to have been a COBOL guy for over 25 years, 
but, I have to admit, when I came to learn new things if I HADN'T learned 
COBOL first it would have been easier. I remember struggling with the new OO 
features in COBOL when they were first released. I put it aside and taught 
myself Java, as if I had never learned anything about computers, right from 
absolute basics (despite having at that time more than 20 years experience 
as a COBOL programmer). Suddenly it all made perfect sense and I went back 
to OO COBOL and had no more problems. It was over a decade later that I 
moved off COBOL completely; OO COBOL components serving me well during that 
time.)

As it is no longer important to me whether a new COBOL standard comes out or 
whether there will be a new release of the compiler with new features in it, 
I really don't mind whether people think COBOL has a future or not, and I 
would say if some people (who are largely coming to the end of their working 
careers), can see their COBOL skills carrying them to the end of their 
careers, that is fine and excellent.

(I wouldn't want to see young people wasting their time on it, though).

OK, acquiring knowledge is seldom a waste of time, but there are priorities.

First you need to make a living and survive and later support a spouse and 
family. Whatever time and fiscal resources you have should be oriented to 
skills that will help to ensure that. If you are working for a company that 
is too tight to contract COBOL skill and they expect you to learn it 
yourself (without offering to pay for your training) so you can support 
legacy (until such time as they decide to pull the rug), my advice would be: 
put your hand down. Don't volunteer. If you are pressed, do your study in 
their time, not yours.

Given I have no personal axe to grind with COBOL, why would I react to 
Taft's article?

Because it insults my intelligence. Because it degrades COBOL and denies the 
valuable service that COBOL rendered for decades, by trying to attach it to 
the coat tails of modern technology. Because it attempts to persuade that 
COBOL is "cool"  (It isn't, but why would it need to be?)Because it doesn't 
tell it like it is. Because it doesn't recognise the changes in the IT 
world, the evolution of a newer paradigm, or even attempt to address WHY 
COBOL is in decline (and it is not because of any particular inherent faults 
in the COBOL language), or what existing COBOLlers who need and expect to be 
working for some decades yet, should be doing about it. (Not just persuading 
themselves that everything is fine and COBOL has a bright future, so there's 
no need to do anything...)

The rate of change in IT is accellerating. (Read Kurzweil's "The Singularity 
is Near" if you want citation as to this...Admittedly his "near" is 2035, 
which ISN'T "near" and will probably not be attained by some of us, but his 
facts and figures are undeniable.)

2015 is 6 years away. I see no reason to withdraw or change my 1995 
statement regarding the use of COBOL by 2015. (In fact, it is closer to 
fruition than I ever expected, already...)

Expand your skill set if you intend to be in IT for the long haul. The days 
when you could make it on COBOL alone are already largely gone.

Get over it.

Move on.

Pete.
```

## Thread: (OT) - Buying advice for new PC (desktop) — 11 this month / 14 total

### (OT) - Buying advice for new PC (desktop)

- **From:** "William M. Klein" <wmklein@nospam.ix.netcom.com>
- **Date:** 2009-09-22T16:20:00-05:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<6cbum.42512$Xg3.33060@en-nntp-04.dc1.easynews.com>`

```
This is one of those cases where the Internet has just TOO MUCH information.  I 
am trying to figure out how to help my sister decide what to buy - for a new 
desktop (tower) computer.  I figured that I state my parameters here and see who 
suggests what.

I will be MORE than happy if someone can point me to a FEW good articles on the 
web - or if you want to email me privately.  I have already checked cnet.com and 
Consumer's Report.

My sister is a "medium computer literate" retired teacher.  She wants a desktop 
(tower) and not a laptop.  She wants to stay with Windows (and she and I both 
know issues related to XP, Vista, and Windows 7).

She primarily uses her computer for:
 - email (via MS Office)
 - Web browsing
 - Preparing of MS Word and Publisher documents
 - Storing (viewing and printing) of LOTS of digital (camera) pictures

She is NOT a "gamer" nor a "programmer" to a home business person.  (She does do 
some MS Excel spread sheets for various groups she is involved in).

She definitely want faster web browsing (she does have Cable internet access) 
and "no worries" about the amount of pictures she stores.  She also would like 
to NOT need to update her computer real soon.  She would also be interested in 
someone else installing the new PC and doing the "transfer" of stuff from the 
old PC.  (She has kept most of the media of programs that she has installed on 
her machine).

She appreciates good (and free or at least cheap) support when she has problems.

She lives in Tucson (if that matters)

 * * * * * *

What suggestions does this group have on:

A) Where I can look to help her make "good decisions"

B) Brands of PCs (and monitors)

C)  What peripherals she needs (especially "back-up" techniques with a large 
(1tb) hard disk

D) Buying from dealer, in store, via web "stores", wherever?

E) Any thing else you can think of.
```

#### ↳ Re: (OT) - Buying advice for new PC (desktop)

- **From:** foodman <foodman123@aol.com>
- **Date:** 2009-09-23T13:06:19-07:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<f9b03410-bc28-4d13-9cae-eeea85374aa4@z34g2000vbl.googlegroups.com>`
- **References:** `<6cbum.42512$Xg3.33060@en-nntp-04.dc1.easynews.com>`

```
Hi Bill:

Just a few comments...

First, all computers are assembled from common components (Intel, AMD,
Seagate, etc.)
so buying a brand name PC doesn't necessarily get you anything special
although
the brand names may offer warranty, support, or other services deemed
valuable.

What you get for your money these days is astonishing, for example:

HP Pavilion a6826f Desktop PC - Intel Core 2 Duo E7400 2.8 GHz, 6GB
DDR2 RAM,
750GB HDD, DVDRW, Vista Home Premium 64 For $499.99!

With the proliferation of digital devices, I would opt for about 8 USB
ports, I currently have a PC with eight and they come in handy for
multiple
memory sticks, cameras, peripherals, etc.

The above is from www.tigerdirect.com. Although I would not recommend
a 64-bit
version of Windows in consideration of some of the older software she
may
have.

It would be easy to just to install the hard drive in her existing PC
into the new one. That way everything would be as it was with the
exception
of the shortcuts which would require changing to reflect the different
drive-letter.  If there were any problems, she has the media anyway if
it were necessary to reinstall for some reason.

Having had a 24-inch monitor for some time now, I STRONGLY recommend
them.
Having much space is very convenient especially if you run multiple
applications simultaneously.  They are wonderful for looking at high-
res
images, too.

I just purchased a 64gb flash drive.  Yes, 64gb in a stick as big as
a
pack of gum. These could be used for backups (don't put all of your
eggs
in one basket) if she gets a 1tb drive which may be overkill. You can
get an
awful lot of JPGs in 64gb.

Check out www.tigerdirect.com, they have huge assortment and are good
to
do business with. Buying-on line is best, in my opinion.

Good Luck with your decision, let us know what she ultimately buys.

Tony Dilworth
```

- **References:** `<6cbum.42512$Xg3.33060@en-nntp-04.dc1.easynews.com> <f9b03410-bc28-4d13-9cae-eeea85374aa4@z34g2000vbl.googlegroups.com>`

```
All good advice; I would point out that external usb/firewire Terrabyte 
drives are often on sale for $99 here in Canada - perhaps less in the US. Of 
course, once you have one TB drive, you feel inclined to get another so that 
you can back up the first one.... and so it goes.  Flash drives have a fixed 
(but likely pretty good) duty cycle - I would prefer to use a 'real' drive 
or drives for backups, but that is just me.

regards
```

#### ↳ Re: (OT) - Buying advice for new PC (desktop)

- **From:** Alistair <alistair@ld50macca.demon.co.uk>
- **Date:** 2009-09-26T05:01:28-07:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<56b2a4b6-4b29-4029-89cd-40a2c7cde352@z28g2000vbl.googlegroups.com>`
- **References:** `<6cbum.42512$Xg3.33060@en-nntp-04.dc1.easynews.com>`

```
I would expect that most machines available in stores would be capable
of meeting your sister's requirements. A few minor points:

1.  Try to get a machine with at least two USB ports in the front
panel. It is a real pain having to reach around to the back of a
machine to remove/insert memory sticks.

2.  If she does anything other than just viewing images (eg editing)
then she would probably be best advised to obtain as much RAM as
possible.

3.  If she junks the old machine and adds the hard disk to the new
machine then the speed of the fastest drive (the new drive) will be
reduced to the same as the old drive (unless UDMA has changed) and
that will be the slowest aspect of her machine after editing large
amounts of digital images in restricted memory spoaces.

4.  She might like to get a video card which has two VDU ports and
obviously two vdus to go with them. That way she can edit two or more
spreadsheets/images without having to swap them in and out of one
screen.


Just in case; to open more than one instance of Excel:
Use the File Association Settings (Explorer)
You have to tell Excel not to use DDE to open the worksheet.
Open Windows Explorer, Tools, Options, File Types
Scroll down to XLS
Select Advance Button
Click on OPEN in the Actions window, Then Edit
On the 2nd line for application used add "%1".
Make sure to put the quotes around %1.
Example ...\Excel.exe" /e "%1"
Write down what you see in the DDE Section.
You will need this information if you want to return to the original
settings.
Now DeSelect Use DDE
When you double click on any XLS file a separate instance of excel
will run.
Another advantage is that you can open more than one XLS file with the
same name
```

#### ↳ Re: (OT) - Buying advice for new PC (desktop)

- **From:** Robert Jones <rjones0@hotmail.com>
- **Date:** 2009-09-27T02:26:44-07:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<155f24b2-63ab-46fe-9c34-2df3e8f389fb@n2g2000vba.googlegroups.com>`
- **References:** `<6cbum.42512$Xg3.33060@en-nntp-04.dc1.easynews.com>`

```
In addition to the comments made by others, I suggest that you try to
get hold of a copy of "Computer Shopper" published in the UK, there
may be another different magazine of the same name in the US.  It
nearly always contains some basic advice with minimum requirements,
together with several reviews of various types of computer, several of
which are also available in the US.  Having said that, the big names
are usually pretty reliable, though there are several good smaller
suppliers.  It is probably a good idea to review several US magazines
to get an idea of what's available and features provided and
desirable.  A local library would probably have copies.

I would suggest that for a long lifetime of use, that you don't get a
too basic version as it will probably need replacing sooner due to
lack of ability to keep up with upgrades.  TV tuners, webcams and
internet phone facilities may be helpful.

I would suggest you ensure that you check the types of port provided,
e.g. USB, Firewire, and anything else you think may be helpful.
Generous RAM and hard disk capacity are also useful for accommodating
upgrades.  USB Flash drives are better for portability of smaller
amounts of data.

I personally use 3 external hard drives for backups, each of 500Gb
capacity, which are kept separately, e.g. one at home, one in the car
and one at another address.  Norton Ghost seems to work reasonably
well as a backup utility, but no doubt there are others.  Internet
backup services are also available, but can take a very long time and
a lot of bandwith for larger volumes of data.  I suggest your sister
keeps the programs and data separate, since the programs once backed
up, wont need doing again till the next upgrade, and the volume of
data for regular backups will be smaller.  Data kept on external hard
drives, etc should be password protected with encryption.  The
computer's own drive should also be encrypted if possible, I believe
the latest versions of Windows makes this very easy to accomplish,
though you must remember to keep the passwords securely, both to
ensure that no one unauthorised gets them and that she doesn't forget
them.  It might be a good idea for her to let you have a copy of her
list, which you could encrypt with your own password.

If you have some good recommendations for local independant suppliers,
then they can be much more responsive and flexible.  Warranties
usually come with some form of maintenance agreement for the first
year or three, some are better than others, some will collect and
return, while others expect you to send the computer yourself.  Some
have return to base warranties, while others will attempt to make
repairs onsite, but usually cost more. You would generally get a
better price for online purchases, but local may be more convenient
and responsive for advice and repairs.  Telephone hotlines can be
expensive.

If your sister has any special peripherals, e.g. scanners, printers,
cameras, etc, then it is advisable to ensure that they will continue
to work and that any special ports that they need are available on the
new machine.

Robert
```

##### ↳ ↳ Re: (OT) - Buying advice for new PC (desktop)

- **From:** docdwarf@panix.com ()
- **Date:** 2009-09-28T13:35:22+00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<h9qe2q$ijb$3@reader1.panix.com>`
- **References:** `<6cbum.42512$Xg3.33060@en-nntp-04.dc1.easynews.com> <155f24b2-63ab-46fe-9c34-2df3e8f389fb@n2g2000vba.googlegroups.com>`

```
In article <155f24b2-63ab-46fe-9c34-2df3e8f389fb@n2g2000vba.googlegroups.com>,
Robert Jones  <rjones0@hotmail.com> wrote:

[snip]

>I personally use 3 external hard drives for backups, each of 500Gb
>capacity, which are kept separately, e.g. one at home, one in the car
>and one at another address.  Norton Ghost seems to work reasonably
>well as a backup utility, but no doubt there are others.

I used to use Norton Ghost and found that after Win95 it became such 
bloatware that I abandoned it in favor of Acronis TrueImage.  Whatever you 
choose make sure that it has the capability of 'bare metal restore' so 
that all you need is a recent backup drive and a boot CD in order to make 
a new, 'naked' machine into an image of the one that went kerflooie.

Hardware is important, true... but data are sacred.

DD
```

- **From:** "Pete Dashwood" <dashwood@removethis.enternet.co.nz>
- **Date:** 2009-09-29T22:30:55+13:00

## Thread: LOW-VALUES to a numeric field — 20 msgs

### LOW-VALUES to a numeric field

- **From:** Graham Hobbs <ghobbs@cdpwise.net>
- **Date:** 2009-09-22T22:23:34-04:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<te1jb5p6rijuld983j7gcj2o0h51qq81il@4ax.com>`

```
Hello,

I have a field in both a VSAM copybook and a DB2 DCLGEN:

05 fld pic s9(5) comp-3.

It will be a key in a CICS program to reach top of file|table.

'move low-values to fld' will not compile.

So two ways I know of are:

a) 
05 fld-r redefines fld pic x(3).
then use 'move low-values to fld-r' 
except it could mean copybook changes, bit dodgier in the case of
automatically generated DCLGEN's, so I am generally anti-copybook
doctoring.

b) 
'move -99999 to fld'
has flaws: it isn't the lowest of the low, is easier to miscode, is
not the very explicit 'low-values'.

I really would like to just do 'move low-values to fld'. Is there a
solution I don't know about?

Thanks
Graham
```

#### ↳ Re: LOW-VALUES to a numeric field

- **From:** Arnold Trembley <arnold.trembley@att.net>
- **Date:** 2009-09-22T22:18:37-05:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<IbKdnZP7OosSDiTXnZ2dnUVZ_v-dnZ2d@giganews.com>`
- **In-Reply-To:** `<te1jb5p6rijuld983j7gcj2o0h51qq81il@4ax.com>`
- **References:** `<te1jb5p6rijuld983j7gcj2o0h51qq81il@4ax.com>`

```
Graham Hobbs wrote:
> Hello,
> 
…[27 more quoted lines elided]…
> 

Can your field as it is used normally contain negative values?  How 
about zero?

Without knowing your application I cannot be sure, but I would recommend:

MOVE ZERO TO FLD.

Even if you could find a way to force low-values into a packed decimal 
field, that's just inviting a S0C7 abend.
```

#### ↳ Re: LOW-VALUES to a numeric field

- **From:** "Pete Dashwood" <dashwood@removethis.enternet.co.nz>
- **Date:** 2009-09-23T16:14:41+12:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<7htllcF2v0g00U1@mid.individual.net>`
- **References:** `<te1jb5p6rijuld983j7gcj2o0h51qq81il@4ax.com>`

```
Graham Hobbs wrote:
> Hello,
>
…[23 more quoted lines elided]…
> solution I don't know about?

Looks like there isn't :-)

Redefines or the lowest legal value just about covers it.

I was shocked when I read your post because most of the mainframers I know 
learned decades ago NEVER to make packed fields key fields, and generally 
(since about the mid-eighties, when inter-system communication  became a 
system design consideration and the cost of storage was dropping 
exponentially) to avoid using packed fields at all (except perhaps for 
currency)

Sure you can do it, but, as you are finding, there are subtle implications 
which are not immediately obvious.

Never mind, you have the situation you have and the best must be made of it.

My vote would be for the -99999 solution.

It lets you use the field legitimately for negative numbers, and has the 
least impact on the COPY books.

Pete.
```

#### ↳ Re: LOW-VALUES to a numeric field

- **From:** riplin <riplin@Azonic.co.nz>
- **Date:** 2009-09-22T22:56:44-07:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<b14c39c5-93b8-45d5-bd46-2aed781dc3bf@j9g2000prh.googlegroups.com>`
- **References:** `<te1jb5p6rijuld983j7gcj2o0h51qq81il@4ax.com>`

```
On Sep 23, 2:23 pm, Graham Hobbs <gho...@cdpwise.net> wrote:
> Hello,
>
…[23 more quoted lines elided]…
> solution I don't know about?

In systems that I use -99999 is not even a low byte value, it is the
highest valid byte value. S9(5) COMP-3 is packed and postsigned. The
only difference between the byte values of +99999 and -99999 is the
final nybble.

ZERO is hex 00000x where x is some value of the sign. -99999 is hex
99999D and +99999 is hex 99999D.

COMP-x fields can only be used where they are used for COMPutations.
Attempting to use these as keys where only the byte value is important
will fail in non-useful ways.
```

##### ↳ ↳ Re: LOW-VALUES to a numeric field

#### ↳ Re: LOW-VALUES to a numeric field

- **From:** "William M. Klein" <wmklein@nospam.ix.netcom.com>
- **Date:** 2009-09-23T04:13:01-05:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<AElum.55443$GS3.38859@en-nntp-07.dc1.easynews.com>`
- **References:** `<te1jb5p6rijuld983j7gcj2o0h51qq81il@4ax.com>`

```
There have already been some useful replies, but I wanted to come back to the OP 
and ask exactly what they are trying to do.

A) Are you trying to set this numeric field to the smallest possible VALID 
value - so that you can start a "browse" of the file from the lowest record 
forward?

B) Are you trying to set the field to some "invalid" value that can never appear 
in a VALID record - to be used as some sort of "flag".

C) something else?

 * * * * *

From your statement,
 "It will be a key in a CICS program to reach top of file|table"

and ignoring the use of "top" of file/table (rather than beginning), then I 
would say that if this field is TRULY a numeric field that should be defined as 
COMP-3, then you should simply move -99999 to it.  You also need to "understand" 
your data to know if this is or is not (ever) a possible valid value for the 
field.  Your processing will be different depending upon that.

 * * * * * *

What you are really looking for, is a new feature in the '02 ANSI/ISO Standard 
that is NOT available in any IBM compiler.  (I am assuming IBM by uses of "VSAM" 
and "DB2" in your original note).  In the current ('02 Standard), you can use 
the intrinsic functions HIGHEST-ALGEBRAIC and LOWEST-ALGEBRAIC to place the 
lowest POSSIBLE VALID value into a numeric field (based on its picture and 
usage).  This works with signed and unsigned fields and with display, national, 
packed-decimal, floating-point, binary, and all other types of fields.

If you are an IBM customer, you can create a "Marketing Request" (via your local 
IBM branch) to request that IBM add support for these intrinsic functions into 
the "soonest possible' FUTURE version of their compiler.  If you don't know how 
to do this, but want to, feel free to contact me off-line.
```

```
Hello Bill Klein,

In my reply to Alistair said I'd lost your post - well I found it.

Your A) covers it exactly. Just from purist reasons I can startbr with
GT (greater than) for alpha keys but need GE (greater than or equal)
for numeric keys. The implication to me being, GT produces a single
result, GE is an 'or'.

Yes I am an IBM customer, so small I don't get/afford 'support'. Such
a new feature in COBOL would be a) useful to me for startbr with a
numeric key, b) kind of conform with low/high values in alpha fields,
c) other than top/end of file CICS browsing via a numeric key I can't
think of another use - maybe in batch?

Other posts (and my thanks for such) confirm what I asked can't be
done. For now I will go with the low/high legal value.

Cheers
Graham
```

```
> Hello Bill Klein,

Hi Graham,

I'm late to the party (maybe too late), but here goes, anyway:

In the FD for the file, code an additional 01, for e.g. "01 other-def
pic x(nnn)." where nnn = the length of the orig-def you receiv- ed
from the cust.

To set the key to X'00's MOVE LOW-VALUES TO other-def(a:b) where a =
the pos of the key in the rec and b = the len of the key.

If your compiler doesn't support reference modifiaction, please ignore
this post.  :-)
```

```
Never too late to party Slade! I like it, never thought of it.

E.G.
      * This is the users copybook
       01  VSAMDATA.
           05 FIVER1                      PIC  X(5).
           05 FIVER2                      PIC  S9(6).
           05 FIVER3                      PIC  S9(5)V9(2) COMP-3.
           05 FIVER4                      PIC  X(5).

      * This is what I create - easy to do, doesn't interfere with
      * users' copybooks, not as pure as Bill Klein's suggested
      * 'new Cobol reequirement', but works for my purposes
       01  VSAMDATA-REDEF REDEFINES VSAMDATA.
           05 FILLER                      PIC  X(5).
           05 FIVER2-A                  PIC  X(6).
           05 FIVER3-A                  PIC  X(4).
           05 FILLER                      PIC  X(5).

      * and then 'move high/low vals to fiver2-a and/or fiver3-a 

So now I have two solutions - my 'full' REDEFINES above or reference
mod as you suggest - which raised an interesting point for me because
when I write pgms I have occasionally used reference mod without
thought to compiler capabilities. More food for thought.
Thanks.
Graham
```

_(thread depth: 5)_

- **From:** "William M. Klein" <wmklein@nospam.ix.netcom.com>
- **Date:** 2009-09-27T21:08:07-05:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol

- **References:** `<te1jb5p6rijuld983j7gcj2o0h51qq81il@4ax.com> <AElum.55443$GS3.38859@en-nntp-07.dc1.easynews.com> <ji6tb55ek0k9qd4ft1bckic6k6765iqmmd@4ax.com> <a8e69e56-6c63-47b0-b26f-5c899aecd5a4@p15g2000vbl.googlegroups.com> <01dvb5tke63394090m7qjgp2pq776mlbnn@4ax.com>`

```
Please, PLEASE, stop responding with ways to get "low-values" into the numeric 
key field. Although the original poster used that term, it was subsequently made 
clear that this was NOT what was really wanted.  What was wanted was the ability 
to put a value that would be the LOWEST value (to start a "sequential" browse of 
a file).

Although "Low-Values would meet such a requirement for an alphanumeric key 
field, it does NOT for a key field that is numeric.  As the OP acknowledge 
moving -999 (for signed) or 000 for unsigned would do this.  (Make the number of 
"9s" correct for the picture clause).

As I previously said, the current COBOL Standard does have support for this.  It 
has the HIGH-ALGEBRAIC and LOWEST-ALGEBRAIC intrinsic functions.  The OP's 
compiler doesn't currently support this, but it is what was mean when the term 
"low-values for numeric field" was used.

FYI,
  If (unlike the OP) one really did want to move low-values to a key field, then 
there is an easy way to do this without any redefines.  Given a copybook of:

>       01  VSAMDATA.
>           05 FIVER1                      PIC  X(5).
>           05 FIVER2                      PIC  S9(6).
>           05 FIVER3                      PIC  S9(5)V9(2) COMP-3.
>           05 FIVER4                      PIC  X(5).

The follow code would do this:
   Move Low-Values to VSAMDATA (12:7)

This doesn't do what the OP *wants* but does do what others are trying to get 
to.
```

###### ↳ ↳ ↳ Re: LOW-VALUES to a numeric field

```
On Sep 28, 3:08 pm, "William M. Klein" <wmkl...@nospam.ix.netcom.com>
wrote:
> Please, PLEASE, stop responding with ways to get "low-values" into the numeric
> key field. Although the original poster used that term, it was subsequently made
…[7 more quoted lines elided]…
> "9s" correct for the picture clause).

Does VSAM differentiate between alphanumeric and numeric parts of a
file key ? If I had an indexed sequential file on my system and a key
had been defined as in the example then I would expect the file system
to treat the key as one 20 character alpha numeric field.

Any negative numbers in the S9(6) DISPLAY NUMERIC or in the COMP-3
field would follow the positive absolute value as the fields are sign
trailing.

So if the file was read sequentially then 'ABCDE00001...' would be
followed by 'ABCDE00000p...' (or whatever -1 was represented as) and
then every other numeric pair of values with the positive of n
followed by the negative of n.

So 'ABCDE99999v..' (or whatever -999999 was) would be the _highest_
value (of the series 'ABCDE...') .

Similarly for the COMP-3 field.

So why, exactly, do you think that using -999.. is useful in any way ?


> As I previously said, the current COBOL Standard does have support for this.  It
> has the HIGH-ALGEBRAIC and LOWEST-ALGEBRAIC intrinsic functions.  The OP's
…[148 more quoted lines elided]…
>
```

- **References:** `<te1jb5p6rijuld983j7gcj2o0h51qq81il@4ax.com> <AElum.55443$GS3.38859@en-nntp-07.dc1.easynews.com> <ji6tb55ek0k9qd4ft1bckic6k6765iqmmd@4ax.com> <a8e69e56-6c63-47b0-b26f-5c899aecd5a4@p15g2000vbl.googlegroups.com> <01dvb5tke63394090m7qjgp2pq776mlbnn@4ax.com> <cUUvm.9541$sz1.5090@en-nntp-10.dc1.easynews.com> <d7p1c5tlnub2eson48l1p9qablsnusi9kr@4ax.com>`

```
Well, ....

You could create a callable module (user-defined function if you had those),

Then,
  Pass it the picture string and usage of the field that you want to receiver 
the highest/lowest possible value (Pass this by content - or by reference)
    and
 Pass it  (by reference) the filed that you want to get the high/low value.

In the subroutine, "parse" the picture string and move the correct value to the 
field.  OBVIOUSLY, this would be semi-tricky for things like
  - floating-point (COMP-1/COMP-2 in IBM environments)
  - binary fields where ANSI conforming TRUNC isn't turned on - but a Picture 
was specified (E.g. IBM TRUNC(OPT) and PIC S9(2) Binary - for example)

  * * * * *

I don't know if it would be "useful enough" to create such a routine, but it 
would do what the '02 Standard intrinsic functions do.
```

```
You can (maybe) avoid the copybook problem with

01  Dumx.
  02  Dumx-9 pic s9(5) comp-3.

MOVE LOW-VALUES TO DUMX.

...

MOVE DUMX-9 TO fld.

Assuming your compiler doesn't check validity on a non-converting move.
```

##### ↳ ↳ Re: LOW-VALUES to a numeric field

- **From:** docdwarf@panix.com ()
- **Date:** 2009-09-24T00:34:01+00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<h9eepo$pe0$1@reader1.panix.com>`
- **References:** `<te1jb5p6rijuld983j7gcj2o0h51qq81il@4ax.com> <paednSY9yNsQDSfXnZ2dnUVZ_qidnZ2d@earthlink.com>`

```
In article <paednSY9yNsQDSfXnZ2dnUVZ_qidnZ2d@earthlink.com>,
HeyBub <heybub@NOSPAMgmail.com> wrote:
>Graham Hobbs wrote:
>> Hello,
…[21 more quoted lines elided]…
>Assuming your compiler doesn't check validity on a non-converting move. 

I think the original advice given was, as paraphrased below, very 
reasonable.

IT IS USUALLY NOT A VERY GOOD IDEA TO MOVE A NON-NUMERIC VALUE TO A PACKED 
NUMERIC (COMP-3) FIELD.

IT IS *SO* USUALLY NOT A VERY GOOD IDEA THAT THE COMPILER WON'T ALLOW YOU 
TO DO IN THIS CASE.

If someone's design is so bad that it requires kludging code to get around 
compiler rules then maybe the design needs to be revisited... and by a 
different designer, one who is not married to the CIO's elderly, ugly 
daughter.

Of course... it is not likely that this'll happen.  The design has already 
been approved by people (who, when pressed, will quite likely and quite 
proudly admit to being 'Not Technical') who are convinced they are right.

I would suggest that you plead ignorance... 'I'd love to do it but the 
compiler just won't let me and I can't figure out a way around it.'  
You'll be ridiculed and the job will be given to someone who will, most 
likely, write some 'Look, Mom, I'm a Programmer!' code to get around this 
design flaw... and when the whole thing comes crashing down at least you 
will have a step or two of remove from it.

(This is how I suggest an employee handles it.  As a 
consultant/contractor/hired gun I would say 'I refuse to write code that 
would allow for such a fundamental flaw to be perpetuated; to do so would 
be a violation of my professional ethics.' I would also be prepared to 
find another job for such a refusal.)

DD
```

#### ↳ Re: LOW-VALUES to a numeric field

- **From:** Alistair <alistair@ld50macca.demon.co.uk>
- **Date:** 2009-09-26T05:12:06-07:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<18794eb4-f64e-4d0e-8b23-e15e5c272652@g1g2000vbr.googlegroups.com>`
- **References:** `<te1jb5p6rijuld983j7gcj2o0h51qq81il@4ax.com>`

```
On Sep 23, 3:23 am, Graham Hobbs <gho...@cdpwise.net> wrote:
> Hello,
>
…[4 more quoted lines elided]…
> It will be a key in a CICS program to reach top of file|table.

I wonder if there is some efficiency implication in using low-values
here? I worked somewhere once where a single high-values record was
added to each VSAM file before loading with the result that the CI and
CA breaks caused a reduction in efficiency when loading data as each
record was inserted before the last (high-values) record.
```

##### ↳ ↳ Re: LOW-VALUES to a numeric field

- **From:** Graham Hobbs <ghobbs@cdpwise.net>
- **Date:** 2009-09-26T14:50:51-04:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<qjmsb5pksfl6fhrdlparcr9ivkb0011jul@4ax.com>`
- **References:** `<te1jb5p6rijuld983j7gcj2o0h51qq81il@4ax.com> <18794eb4-f64e-4d0e-8b23-e15e5c272652@g1g2000vbr.googlegroups.com>`

```
Don't know about that Alistair. Since my original post four days ago
my machine went down and I lost some replies. One I remember from Bill
Klein asked about context so ...

Scenario is I get copybooks from clients, maybe DB2 maybe VSAM, maybe
numeric keys usually not, some suave some not. I write pgms to put the
table or file online via CICS where browsing up and down the file or
table is required, e.g. entering a new key, top/end of file (tof/eof),
up/down 'n' recs. 

In particular tof and eof are vastly simplified by using the lowest or
highest possible value in the startbr command where fld is the key so:

If fld is pic xxx the startbr is
   if tof
      move low-values to fld and readnext's
   else
   if eof
      move high-values to fld and readprev's
   end
.
This is the normal and satisfactory solution albeit based on the usual
situation that files/tables don't have extraneous high/low value recs.

However, if fld is pic 999 or s999 the startbr is
   if tof
      compute fld = -999 (or 000 if unsigned) and readnext's
   else
   if eof
      compute fld = 999 and readprev's
   end
.
It is this numeric method that is 'not as ultimate' because you can't
move low/high vals to a numeric field
UNLESS 
there is something I don't know ... very possible.

Because I work with client copybooks I am not interested in adding
redefines stmts. So the solution needs to be in the procedure code.

So other than -999 and +999 for a signed fld or 000 and 999 for an
unsigend field, any other ideas?

Graham

On Sat, 26 Sep 2009 05:12:06 -0700 (PDT), Alistair
<alistair@ld50macca.demon.co.uk> wrote:

>On Sep 23, 3:23ï¿½am, Graham Hobbs <gho...@cdpwise.net> wrote:
>> Hello,
…[11 more quoted lines elided]…
>record was inserted before the last (high-values) record.
```

<a id="t-addc49466f"></a>
## Thread: When are "users" using COBOL — 5 this month / 6 total

### When are "users" using COBOL

- **From:** "William M. Klein" <wmklein@nospam.ix.netcom.com>
- **Date:** 2009-09-24T21:00:55-05:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<uvVum.62661$3D4.20019@en-nntp-05.dc1.easynews.com>`

```
As a follow-up on another thread, I just thought I would try to start a POSITIVE 
list of when "real world" people MAY (unknowingly) being "using" COBOL today. 
(This is not intended to COMPARE when they are using COBOL vs Java, C3, PL/I, 
Fortran, VB, or any other language).  This is, in part, based on what 
"companies" are still active in SHARE, IBM's z/os (mostly) mainframe user group.

- Using a credit or debit card
- Using an ATM
- Possibly, when doing an online account inquiry or transaction
 - Using their land-line phone (for billing - unless they are on a "fixed" 
plan) - I don't know about cell phone company billing.
 - (continuously) when using Gas or Oil to heat their home or business (again, 
for billing)
 - Receiving and paying an insurance bill
 - (possibly) when filing or following up on an insurance "incident"
 - Making, changing, or checking on a plane or train reservation
 - dealing with the government (state or federal - probably, local - possibly)
 - Often when you "expect" a store to be "stocked" with some item that you want

*OBVIOUSLY* not all such "interactions" use COBOL for all 
companies/organization, but my perception is that these ALL still have a 
majority that involve COBOL in one or more parts of the interaction.
```

#### ↳ Re: When are "users" using COBOL

- **From:** Rene_Surop <infodynamics_ph@yahoo.com>
- **Date:** 2009-09-29T18:48:04-07:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<7020ec92-f840-49a0-868e-5e9e1318e805@h40g2000prf.googlegroups.com>`
- **References:** `<uvVum.62661$3D4.20019@en-nntp-05.dc1.easynews.com>`

```
From my side; I had a first hand product and co-develop several Cobol
systems on the following;

1.  POS/Point-of-sale (Grocery & department retail store application;
pure Cobol)
2.  Credit Card processing (Commercial bank; Cobol 80% Java 20%)
3.  Insurance Company (Life Support Plus product; Synon/Cobol 90% VB
5% Java 5%)
4.  Government Agency (Billing & Collection; pure Cobol)
5.  Water Districts (Billing & Collection; Cobol 90% ASP/VBscript/
XHTML 10%)
6.  Automotive Industry (Parts and Service apps; Cobol 70% Sybase
Powerbuilder 20% VBscript/ASP/XHTML)
6.  Online Appliance Retailing (Invty, A/R, A/P; Cobol 95% ASP/
VBscript/XHTML/AJAX 5%)

The companies that are using these apps are considered big corp and
medium-based sizes.

P.S.
In behalf of my company (iNFO Dynamics), we would like to thank those
international groups (NGOs) who helped in the Philippines flooding
rescue and recovery. Thank you very much.
```

##### ↳ ↳ Re: When are "users" using COBOL

- **From:** "don@higgins.net" <don@higgins.net>
- **Date:** 2009-09-30T02:47:23-07:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<92ec052b-9776-4d65-98bc-7669817039b0@t32g2000yqj.googlegroups.com>`
- **References:** `<uvVum.62661$3D4.20019@en-nntp-05.dc1.easynews.com> <7020ec92-f840-49a0-868e-5e9e1318e805@h40g2000prf.googlegroups.com>`

```
Bill, all

Another application everyone is using is customer service for electric
utilities.  I spent 25 years with Florida Power in IT.  They had COBOL
billing and payroll running on OS/MFT when I got there, and they had
EXEC CICS and batch COBOL with DB2 running when I left to join Micro
Focus.  From 1992-1995 I worked on CSS project to implement new GUI
client server customer system and the server side was still EXEC CICS
COBOL and batch on MVS.  That server side customer service system
architecture with COBOL was jointly developed with Accenture, and has
been deployed on over 30$ of all US electric utility companies:

http://don-higgins.com/css.htm

COBOL is very much alive and well, but mostly behind the scenes
processing transactions.

Don Higgins
don@higgins.net
www.zcobol.org
```

###### ↳ ↳ ↳ Re: When are "users" using COBOL

- **From:** Rene_Surop <infodynamics_ph@yahoo.com>
- **Date:** 2009-09-30T17:42:22-07:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<000c5703-4aa9-4ab7-b86f-ad085cfb3322@y28g2000prd.googlegroups.com>`
- **References:** `<uvVum.62661$3D4.20019@en-nntp-05.dc1.easynews.com> <7020ec92-f840-49a0-868e-5e9e1318e805@h40g2000prf.googlegroups.com> <ha0pju$32d$1@svr7.m-online.net>`

```
> How do you measure that? LoC or what? I can easily change any statistic
> of that kind to whatever I want. It this means (as I  suppose) these 80%
…[3 more quoted lines elided]…
> Jessica

I don't measure it, and at any point in time I didn't do stats on it.

Referring to the topic, what I have is a fact on my side. I first-hand
coded some of the Cobol source code so I knew how those products
evolve within their company. Created the POS (point-of-sale) myself
and it's pure Cobol. All Cobol codes are back and front-end solutions.
If you look at the 'heavy' applications we are using, I could say that
Cobol is still growing.

Having said that; a pure (or combination) VB, C#, Java or other
languages maybe running on THE SAME apps in other companies so we
never really can't tell unless their is a ruling organization that
handles computerization projects that carries out stats figure.
```
